201412	955	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	President Rosengren.	13	1
201412	956	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201412	957	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	As we began expanding our balance sheet in 2008 and 2009, one of the biggest concerns raised was that such a policy would be inflationary.	13	1
201412	958	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Yet six years later, one of the major problems confronting the economy remains an inflation rate that is too low, and this even at a time when the unemployment rate is approaching some estimates of the natural rate.	13	1
201412	959	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	In fact, if one focused on the consistently strong payroll employment growth over the past six months, the unemployment rate at 5.8 percent, and the forecast of real GDP growth in excess of potential growth, one might feel policy should lift off relatively soon.	13	1
201412	960	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	However, such an analysis would ignore the critical facts that current wage and price growth are significantly below levels consistent with our announced 2 percent inflation target.	13	1
201412	961	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Moreover, my own forecast does not have us reaching a core PCE inflation rate of 2 percent any time soon.	13	1
201412	962	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	One possible explanation for the weakness in wages and prices is that labor markets have more slack than a cursory assessment would indicate.	13	1
201412	963	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Because of the disruptions that occurred during the recession, it is quite possible that a U-3 unemployment rate, by itself, underestimates the amount of labor market slack.	13	1
201412	964	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	With U-6 and long-term unemployment still elevated, defining full employment with U-3 historical estimates may be why we are still seeing unusually low wage and price inflation, even as U-3 approaches a value that many deem to be consistent with full employment.	13	1
201412	965	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Another possibility is that the U-3 rate consistent with full employment is lower than our current estimates.	13	1
201412	966	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	My own estimate of full employment is 5¼ percent.	13	1
201412	967	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Before the recession, my estimate was a shade under 5 percent.	13	1
201412	968	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	If the past 40 years have taught us anything, it is that the natural rate moves around.	13	1
201412	969	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Even relative to 2007, the labor force has become older and more educated.	13	1
201412	970	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Older and more educated workers tend to experience lower unemployment rates.	13	1
201412	971	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Other things being equal, this would be consistent with a slightly lower level of the equilibrium unemployment rate than my current estimate of 5¼ percent.	13	1
201412	972	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thus, as the unemployment rate declines with little evidence of wage and price pressure, in aggregate or by occupational grouping, I am likely to soon reduce my estimate of full employment to make it more consistent with the absence of wage and price pressures we are experiencing.	13	1
201412	973	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	It is quite possible that even if there are developing price pressures, they will not be obvious in the data by the middle of next year.	13	1
201412	974	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	The Tealbook forecast has total and core PCE inflation for the second quarter of next year at 1.4 percent and the ECI at 2.8 percent for all four quarters of 2015.	13	1
201412	975	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	If this is close to the actual outcomes, we will have little evidence of progress toward our 2 percent inflation goal based on wage and price data even by the middle of next year.	13	1
201412	976	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	The very low wage and price pressures pose a challenge for deciding when liftoff should occur.	13	1
201412	977	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	One reason is that downward nominal wage rigidity may be complicating the signal that one can reasonably draw about labor market slack from current wage developments.	13	1
201412	978	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Because many businesses did not cut nominal wages outright during the recession or in the earlier part of the recovery as equilibrium wages declined, we may now be observing slower wage growth to compensate for the earlier lack of downward adjustment.	13	1
201412	979	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	One way to overcome this difficulty is to look at the wages of new hires, which are typically more sensitive to business cycle conditions than the wages of existing employees.	13	1
201412	980	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	New-hire wages could potentially be a leading indicator of emerging labor market tightness.	13	1
201412	981	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	My staff has been analyzing the monthly wage file from the CPS.	13	1
201412	982	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	After controlling for demographic features of the data, they find that in previous recoveries, new-hire wages did grow significantly faster than existing employee wages.	13	1
201412	983	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	However, to date in the current recovery, that pattern has yet to emerge strongly in the data.	13	1
201412	984	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thus, unlike previous recoveries, they are not yet seeing much evidence of wage pressures and that is consistent with there still being significant labor market slack.	13	1
201412	985	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Needless to say, it is important not to focus solely on one indicator when assessing price and wage pressures and their relationship with the extent of slack in the economy.	13	1
201412	986	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Prices are affected by variables other than past wage movements.	13	1
201412	987	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Hence, they can move before wages.	13	1
201412	988	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Furthermore, the statistical relationship between aggregate wages and most real measures of labor market slack is not always stable.	13	1
201412	989	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Finally, because of recent exchange rate and oil price shocks, it may be particularly difficult to determine underlying wage and price trends.	13	1
201412	990	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Still, at least so far, the bulk of evidence appears consistent with little incipient inflationary pressures.	13	1
201412	991	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	In this context, there appears to be ample reason for patience.	13	1
201412	992	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	That is particularly true given the disinflation in Europe and Japan and the recent turbulence generated by sharply lower oil prices, which calls into question the robustness of a global recovery.	13	1
201412	993	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	However, it would be important to parse incoming wage and price data carefully.	13	1
201412	994	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	The very low breakevens and five- year Treasury rates well below 2 percent, even though most investors expect us to tighten starting next year, indicate that we are still in danger of undermining our credibility on our inflation target.	13	1
201412	995	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	The European quandary highlights why we should not take this risk lightly.	13	1
201412	996	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	All of the above provide ample reason to probe the degree of labor market slack further and to look for signs that we can confidently expect to move back to our inflation target over the forecast horizon.	13	1
201412	997	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1

201412	1067	2014-12-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	As labor market conditions continue to improve, the question of what constitutes maximum employment becomes a more pressing topic that President Lacker already talked about.	13	1
201412	1068	2014-12-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Distinguishing between structural and cyclical factors in labor markets is essential to this question, and my staff, like others in the System, as already mentioned, have been working to provide some answers to this question.	13	1
201412	1069	2014-12-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	One structural factor that’s been a concern of late is job polarization, which refers to the disappearance of middle-skill, routine jobs that are replaced by computer-based technologies or are offshored.	13	1
201412	1070	2014-12-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Although this process has been ongoing for three decades now, it accelerated during the recent recession and may have left a sizable number of routine jobs permanently dislocated.	13	1
201412	1071	2014-12-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	My staff examined the extent to which this type of structural job loss has contributed to the mismatch and pushed up the natural rate of unemployment during the latest downturn and recovery.	13	1
201412	1072	2014-12-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	They found only minimal effects, largely consistent with earlier research conducted by the staff of the New York Fed.	13	1
201412	1073	2014-12-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Workers in routine jobs have seen a pickup in their job-finding rates similar to workers with more favored nonroutine jobs, and, more generally, job mismatches associated with polarization appear to be limited, boosting the unemployment rate by only ¼ percentage point at most.	13	1
201412	1074	2014-12-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	To further probe the role of mismatch, my staff also updated their earlier work on the interaction between the Beveridge curve and aggregate labor demand, as reflected in the job creation curve, and their results, which encompass a full range of sources of mismatch, also shows a limited effect of mismatch today.	13	1
201412	1075	2014-12-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Combined, these findings and the other research that was done in recent years on this topic add to my confidence that the long-term natural rate has not risen by a significant amount in the aftermath of the recession.	13	1

201412	1102	2014-12-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	In the Survey of Professional Forecasters, long-term expectations of PCE and price inflation have been glued to 2 percent—that’s 2.0 percent—over the past two years.	13	1
201412	1103	2014-12-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	That sounds like success to me.	13	1
201412	1104	2014-12-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Although CPI long-run inflation expectations have come down a touch, analysis by my staff suggests that this is much ado about nothing.	13	1

201412	1114	2014-12-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Now, of course, market-based measures of expected inflation and associated risks, in particular breakeven inflation rates, have come down by more than the survey-based measures.	13	1
201412	1115	2014-12-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	However, consistent with the findings noted in the Tealbook, a model developed by my staff at the San Francisco Fed attributes these declines to risk and liquidity premiums rather than expected inflation.	13	1
201412	1116	2014-12-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	That brings us to President Kocherlakota and his staff’s memo—which I thought was very thought-provoking and very insightful—that basically made the point that we should not distinguish between these two components, meaning inflation expectations and the inflation risk premium.	13	1
201412	1117	2014-12-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	According to the memo, we should simply react to the full inflation compensation in order to account for market participants’ valuation of the risks associated with different inflation outcomes.	13	1
201412	1118	2014-12-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Now, despite the theoretical elegance of his argument, and also my staff’s being thrilled to be able to talk about market-based probabilities and statistically estimated probabilities during the FOMC briefing, I am unconvinced that market prices likely reflect the preferences of American households in the way that the memo lays out.	13	1
201412	1119	2014-12-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	One reason is that a large share of American households doesn’t actively participate in financial markets.	13	1
201412	1120	2014-12-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Indeed, the marginal investor could well be a foreign hedge fund, which would invalidate the welfare rationale for using market prices.	13	1
201412	1121	2014-12-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Certainly, part of the recent decline in breakeven rates reflects a flight to safety from abroad into nominal Treasuries.	13	1
201412	1122	2014-12-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	More generally, as highlighted by the field of behavioral finance, there are a variety of reasons why sentiment and other factors and frictions not associated with marginal utility might influence market prices.	13	1
201412	1123	2014-12-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Furthermore, if the real world did approximate the framework of the full participation in complete markets assumed in the Minneapolis Fed’s memo, one implication of that is that our large-scale asset purchase programs would be ineffective.	13	1
201412	1124	2014-12-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Without some imperfect substitutability among assets, such purchases would have no economic effects through portfolio balance channels.	13	1
201412	1125	2014-12-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	My reading of the available evidence suggests that’s not the world that we live in.	13	1
201412	1126	2014-12-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	For these reasons, I remain convinced that it makes sense, in theory, to consider inflation expectations as well as the risk premium associated with inflation separately.	13	1
201412	1127	2014-12-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	But that’s in theory.	13	1
201412	1128	2014-12-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	In practice, of course, we have imperfect tools to distinguish between these signals.	13	1
201412	1129	2014-12-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Given these measurement difficulties, we should not be too cavalier about the decline in breakeven inflation and should continue to monitor and analyze it and other measures carefully.	13	1

201412	1134	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201412	1135	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I thank President Williams and his staff for his close attention to the Minneapolis Fed memo, although I would recommend—some of the sections that occur later in the memo on limited participation and incomplete markets might address some of the concerns that you raise in your remarks.	13	1
201412	1136	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think a general point would be that we were trying to make—we may not have made it as clearly as we could have—is that it’s important to take into account relative valuations of resources across states of the world as well as the likelihood of those states of the world occurring.	13	1
201412	1137	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Basically, using probabilities alone is akin to counting up GDP by counting up how much things weigh as opposed to using values instead because, basically, probabilities don’t take into account how much people actually value the resources in those different states of the world where you need to have a price to do that.	13	1
201412	1138	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Now, as President Williams and his staff pointed out, I think there are definitely issues about how well financial market prices—and we tried to talk about some of that in the memo— measure exactly marginal valuations for everybody in the economy.	13	1
201412	1139	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think there are reasons to think they are relatively close, but that we can argue about.	13	1
201412	1140	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think we should keep in mind that just looking at probabilities alone is not sufficient, because we want to know how much people value resources, not just how likely states of the world are.	13	1

201412	1149	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Neither the falling price of gasoline nor the rising dollar has yet materially affected the pace of business activity, although we heard acknowledgement that both will come into play in 2015.	13	1
201412	1150	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	I might add that one director talked about the gasoline price having an effect on the composition of sales.	13	1
201412	1151	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	The largest national auto retailer spoke about the preference of Americans now for SUVs and light trucks.	13	1
201412	1152	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	He said, “Don’t listen to what the American public says.	13	1
201412	1153	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	They say they want broccoli, but they want to buy a donut.”	13	1
201412	1154	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	[Laughter]	13	1
201412	1155	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	We had over 300 responses in response to the Board of Governors employment survey.	13	1
201412	1156	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	For us, almost 60 percent of respondents said they intend to increase employment over the next 12 months.	13	1
201412	1157	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	A significant plurality cited expected growth and sales as the most important factor pushing them to hire.	13	1
201412	1158	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	We heard comments that higher turnover is beginning to present problems.	13	1
201412	1159	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Compensation growth, while still generally subdued, appears to be firming.	13	1
201412	1160	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Comments on transport and logistics challenges were worthy of note.	13	1
201412	1161	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Contacts expressed some concern about the growing vulnerability of the economy to transportation bottlenecks.	13	1
201412	1162	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	They cited the shortage of truck drivers and railcars as well as the Long Beach Port congestion.	13	1
201412	1163	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	We heard the view that transportation problems are likely to get worse.	13	1
201412	1164	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Our reports from District contacts evidence rising confidence.	13	1
201412	1165	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Most interpretations of recent national data, both inside the Fed and externally, emphasize the strength of the data, so the cautious contrarian in me says, “Don’t get carried away.”	13	1
201412	1166	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Let me mention some cautionary points on the current and near-term situation.	13	1
201412	1167	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Tracking estimates of fourth-quarter GDP growth, including hours, point to a marked slowdown from well over 4 percent annualized third-quarter growth to down around 2½ percent this quarter.	13	1
201412	1168	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Recent inflation readings remain well below the Committee’s target, with little evidence of acceleration.	13	1
201412	1169	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Headline inflation numbers will likely be extremely soft in the first quarter, with widening divergence of headline and core.	13	1
201412	1170	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	How to explain the declining market- based indications of inflation expectations is not, in my opinion, a closed debate.	13	1
201412	1171	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Payroll jobs growth is certainly quite strong and encouraging.	13	1
201412	1172	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	But considering the level of U-6, the still elevated U-3/U-6 differential, and continuing weak wage growth, I still see a fair measure of employment slack remaining.	13	1
201412	1173	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	These are just cautionary comments.	13	1
201412	1174	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	My baseline forecast submitted for this meeting has not substantially changed from October and September.	13	1
201412	1175	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	My central assumption is that the economy will continue to enjoy an underlying run rate of growth around 3 percent.	13	1
201412	1176	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	In that respect, my forecast sees stronger growth than the December Tealbook by more than ½ percentage point.	13	1
201412	1177	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	I adjusted down my headline inflation projection over the next year, reflecting the playing through of the drop in oil prices.	13	1
201412	1178	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	I have core inflation slightly above the Tealbook over the forecast horizon but do not have core or headline inflation reaching target until 2017.	13	1
201412	1179	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	As regards risks to my outlook, I share the view that substantially lower gasoline and energy prices will likely produce a clear benefit to the real economy in the medium term.	13	1
201412	1180	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	My staff did some statistical modeling of the effect of lower oil prices.	13	1
201412	1181	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	This work suggested positive consumption and investment effects materializing in the second half of 2015.	13	1
201412	1182	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	However, the share of oil and gas structures investment, as a percentage of total investment in structures, has grown significantly since the mid-1990s.	13	1
201412	1183	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	As a consequence, the effect of sustained low oil prices on drilling activity could be a slight drag on growth in the near term.	13	1
201412	1184	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	A second risk to my outlook relates to the impact of a stronger dollar on net exports in the context of weak global growth.	13	1
201412	1185	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	The Tealbook seems to have incorporated effects of these factors into their baseline growth forecast.	13	1
201412	1186	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	I have not yet done so.	13	1
201412	1187	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Given the structure of US exports, I don’t feel I am on firm ground estimating the downside effect of the higher dollar on exports.	13	1
201412	1188	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	I am also uncertain about the second-quarter positive effects on our economy, of what one would expect to be stronger export performance growth and ultimate demand in economies whose currency has depreciated.	13	1
201412	1189	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	I found the exercise of projecting economic conditions at liftoff to be quite useful.	13	1
201412	1190	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Like the Tealbook, I can imagine circumstances leading up to liftoff when the incoming data and near- term outlook could be very short of our mandated objectives.	13	1
201412	1191	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Assuming a mid-2015 liftoff date, our communications in anticipation of liftoff will probably begin as early as the March FOMC meeting.	13	1
201412	1192	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	At this time, it is likely, in my view, that headline PCE inflation will be moving sharply away from our longer-term objective.	13	1
201412	1193	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	The decline in oil prices to date could contribute to negative headline inflation through the February PCE price report.	13	1
201412	1194	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	At the same time, we could be looking at a two-quarter growth rate for this quarter and next, well below the average of the second and third quarters of 2014.	13	1
201412	1195	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	My point is that the array of data relative to mandate could be confidence challenging and require that the Committee look through, discount, and explain away aspects of the picture presented by the data.	13	1
201412	1196	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	This could be an awkward place to be as we approach liftoff.	13	1
201412	1197	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	I will pick up on this thought again in the policy round.	13	1
201412	1198	2014-12-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1

201412	1201	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201412	1202	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	My overall view is that the economy is building momentum in terms of output and employment.	13	1
201412	1203	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	The Fourth District economy continues to expand.	13	1
201412	1204	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	Fifty percent of our contacts reported an improvement in business conditions over the past six to eight weeks compared with 10 percent that reported a deterioration.	13	1
201412	1205	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	This yields an implied diffusion index of 40, slightly less than the 47 we saw at the time of our previous meeting but significantly higher than the 10 we saw last December.	13	1
201412	1206	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	Fourth District business contacts remain optimistic about the economy.	13	1
201412	1207	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	Indeed, over half plan to increase capital spending next year.	13	1
201412	1208	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	In many cases, this investment is being made to expand capacity rather than merely replace depreciated equipment.	13	1
201412	1209	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	Conditions in District labor markets have also improved further.	13	1
201412	1210	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	For the year to date, employment growth has picked up to 1.4 percent, the closest the region has come to the nation’s growth rate in several years.	13	1
201412	1211	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	Anecdotal reports on hiring plans for the coming year continue to indicate steadily improving labor markets.	13	1
201412	1212	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	The unemployment rate for the four states in our District fell to 5.3 percent in October, down almost 1½ percentage points since the end of last year.	13	1
201412	1213	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	The decline in unemployment, the pickup in employment growth, and anecdotal reports of increased plans to hire all paint a favorable labor market picture for the Fourth District.	13	1
201412	1214	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	We do not yet see much evidence of broad wage or price pressures either up or down.	13	1
201412	1215	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	My directors continue to report that wage gains are moderate in the 2 to 3 percent range, on average.	13	1
201412	1216	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	Manufacturers reported that lower-skilled production jobs are readily filled without significant wage growth.	13	1
201412	1217	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	However, we also continue to receive reports of wage pressures increasing for hard-to-find skills and also in high-cost locations.	13	1
201412	1218	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	In general, prices for finished goods remain stable, although we have received reports of higher nonlabor input costs, such as freight charges, despite the lower fuel costs.	13	1
201412	1219	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	My view of the national economy is little changed since the previous meeting.	13	1
201412	1220	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	Incoming information has largely been positive and has given me more confidence that momentum is increasing.	13	1
201412	1221	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	Growth is picking up, and labor markets continue to improve.	13	1
201412	1222	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	We see this across a broad range of indicators, including payroll and household employment, and job openings and quits in JOLTS, which are trending higher and have recently hit multiyear highs.	13	1
201412	1223	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	The percentage of the labor force employed part time for economic reasons remains elevated relative to the period from about 1995 until the crisis, but it, too, has declined significantly and stands at the level we saw in the early 1990s.	13	1
201412	1224	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	There are even tentative signs from the employment cost index that wage gains may be starting to pick up.	13	1
201412	1225	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	Over the intermeeting period, headline inflation has moved further below our target of 2 percent, driven by the sharp decline in oil prices.	13	1
201412	1226	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	This change in prices partly reflects weaker global demand, but most analyses indicate that it has been driven mainly by supply changes.	13	1
201412	1227	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	So far there’s been little pass-through to core inflation measures, which have remained relatively stable.	13	1
201412	1228	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	I’m not anticipating much pass-through because, although results vary across studies, most of the research, including that by the Cleveland Fed staff, suggests that pass-through of energy price shocks to core inflation has been fairly muted since the 1990s.	13	1
201412	1229	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	On balance, lower oil prices should be a net positive for the US economy, although a fair amount of media attention is focused on the negative effects on domestic oil producers.	13	1
201412	1230	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	So long as inflation expectations remain anchored, the appropriate monetary policy response to a negative oil supply shock would not be to increase the level of accommodation.	13	1
201412	1231	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	Indeed, the positive effect on growth from the drop in oil prices will point to slightly tighter policy being appropriate.	13	1
201412	1232	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	Of course, this is dependent on inflation expectations remaining anchored.	13	1
201412	1233	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	I do not find the declines we’ve seen in some of the market-based inflation compensation measures as that troubling yet.	13	1
201412	1234	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	So far the changes in expectations are within the ranges we’ve seen in recent years and partly reflect changes in liquidity and risk premiums.	13	1
201412	1235	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	The Cleveland Fed’s 10-year CPI inflation expectations measure, which was mentioned earlier, has remained quite stable near 2 percent.	13	1
201412	1236	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	Survey measures like the SPF have also been stable, and as the Board staff indicates, the decline in the medium-run inflation expectations measure from the Michigan survey could be reflecting the sharp drop in oil prices rather than a sustained drop in inflation expectations.	13	1
201412	1237	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	I do think we need to keep our eyes on inflation developments.	13	1
201412	1238	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	We also should remember that inflation expectations are endogenous.	13	1
201412	1239	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	To the extent that we believe that the downward pressure on inflation is transitory, we should make sure that message is conveyed.	13	1
201412	1240	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	My outlook remains positive.	13	1
201412	1241	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	I continue to project GDP growth to be about 3 percent over the next couple of years before returning to trend growth of 2½ percent in 2017.	13	1
201412	1242	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	The factors supporting above-trend growth include highly accommodative monetary policy, improving household and business balance sheets and confidence, and strengthening labor markets.	13	1
201412	1243	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	As the expansion continues, I expect the unemployment rate to continue to decline over the forecast horizon, slightly undershooting and then returning to 5½ percent, my estimate of the longer-run unemployment rate, in 2017.	13	1
201412	1244	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	Lower oil and commodity prices will temporarily lower headline inflation, but as these prices stabilize, the economy continues to expand at a slightly above-trend pace, and longer-term inflation expectations remain stable.	13	1
201412	1245	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	I project inflation to gradually rise to our 2 percent objective by the end of 2016.	13	1
201412	1246	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	My projections are dependent on appropriate monetary policy, which, in my view, should reflect actual and projected progress toward the Committee objectives, including the speed with which progress is being made.	13	1
201412	1247	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	I believe we should recognize the substantial progress we’ve made toward our goal of full employment.	13	1
201412	1248	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	I expect that progress to continue, perhaps at an accelerated pace.	13	1
201412	1249	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	Under these conditions, a key condition informing my expected liftoff of the fed funds rate from the zero lower bound is when projected inflation between one and two years ahead reaches the Committee’s goal of 2 percent.	13	1
201412	1250	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	My projection continues to show us reaching this liftoff condition in the first quarter of 2015, and I’ve incorporated this into my projections.	13	1
201412	1251	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	After liftoff, as the expansion continues at an above-trend rate in my projection, I believe it will be appropriate to raise interest rates gradually for a time, similar to a path suggested by a Taylor 1999 rule with inertia, but then to raise rates at a pace more in line with a less inertial Taylor rule.	13	1
201412	1252	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	There continue to be a number of risks to the forecast, but I view these as balanced.	13	1
201412	1253	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	The recent volatility in private financial markets, driven by the drop in oil prices, has a potential for broader spillovers.	13	1
201412	1254	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	Also, conditions abroad may have worsened since our October meeting.	13	1
201412	1255	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	On the other hand, there also seem to be better prospects now for an effective policy response in key economies there, including the euro area.	13	1
201412	1256	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	On the positive side, US growth and employment may be picking up at a faster pace than projected, which suggests we’re getting close to liftoff, and we should remain focused on preparing the public for it.	13	1
201412	1257	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	I’m not sure the public understands that forward-looking monetary policy means it will be appropriate to begin reducing the degree of policy accommodation when the outlook calls for future inflation to be at our goal even though trailing headline inflation is below our goal, and, similarly, when the unemployment rate is not yet at its estimated long-run level.	13	1
201412	1258	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	Indeed, the SEP indicates that all but one participant sees inflation below 2 percent at the time of liftoff, and all but five see inflation at 1 percent or less at the time of liftoff.	13	1
201412	1259	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	In our desire to clarify that we take the downside risk to inflation very seriously, we may have conveyed less of the consensus view that the effect of the oil price shock on inflation is likely to be transitory, and that lower oil prices are likely to be a net positive for the US economy.	13	1
201412	1260	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	I’m concerned that people have taken too negative a read of our views and haven’t fully appreciated the positive developments.	13	1

201412	1265	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201412	1266	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	The Eighth District economy continued to expand during the intermeeting period.	13	1
201412	1267	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	The unemployment rate across District MSAs dropped to 6.0 percent during the most recent reporting period, just 0.2 higher than the national unemployment rate.	13	1
201412	1268	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	Before the 2007–09 recession, the District unemployment rate tended to run slightly higher than the national average.	13	1
201412	1269	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	During much of the past five years, however, the national unemployment rate was notably higher than what we measured in the Eighth District.	13	1
201412	1270	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	The fact that these two rates have returned to their historical relationship during 2014 can be taken as a sign of a return to normalcy in US labor markets.	13	1

201412	1275	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	First-quarter expectations suggest an upward movement in prices with about half of business contacts expecting to keep prices unchanged and 34 percent expecting to increase them.	13	1
201412	1276	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	I took this to indicate deflation is not imminent.	13	1

201412	1280	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	We are hearing continuing reports of serious congestion problems in the national railway system, tending to slow down service and push up costs, as President Lockhart alluded to.	13	1
201412	1281	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	A logistics firm that hires tens of thousands of temporary workers during the holiday season said it expects to keep more of these workers on after the holidays than it has in the past.	13	1
201412	1282	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	I found these anecdotal reports encouraging.	13	1
201412	1283	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	For the national economy, in my view the story continues to be that the US economy has considerable momentum and is being further aided by two tailwinds:  a lower rate structure as compared with several months ago and a sharp drop in oil and gasoline prices.	13	1
201412	1284	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	For the momentum part of the story, we can consider that GDP growth has likely been in excess of 4 percent at an annual rate over the second and third quarters of 2014, and that many private- sector tracking estimates of current-quarter GDP growth are running about 3 percent.	13	1
201412	1285	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	Based on my discussions with CEO District contacts, I think there may be some upside risk to the 3 percent number, so that early next year we could be looking at three very strong GDP growth quarters in a row.	13	1
201412	1286	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	Commensurate with this robust performance, labor markets have been improving more rapidly than many around this table anticipated.	13	1
201412	1287	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	Unemployment will likely continue to tick down and is within just a few jobs reports of the Committee’s central tendency for the long-run value of this important variable.	13	1
201412	1288	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	In addition, some recent reports on retail sales, consumer confidence, and industrial production seem to confirm a narrative of substantial economic strength.	13	1
201412	1289	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	Based on the performance of the real economy alone, my judgment is that the Committee can no longer justify its continued zero-rate policy.	13	1
201412	1290	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	These data are far too hot to rationalize what was really an unprecedented emergency policy in reaction to a very severe crisis.	13	1
201412	1291	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	Even for those who think my characterization of the US economy is too rosy, I think that the most that can be said is that the Committee should perhaps be running a policy with rates somewhat below normal, but not pinned down all the way to the floor at zero.	13	1
201412	1292	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	Even as we begin to normalize the policy rate next year, monetary policy will likely remain very accommodative for several years.	13	1
201412	1293	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	The real economy is strongly signaling that we need to get on with this process before it gets away from us and causes us to take more drastic action later or possibly face a new crisis.	13	1
201412	1294	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	I might also remark that, in terms of goal variables, if you take unemployment and inflation and you put a quadratic objective on them and look at how far inflation is from target and how far unemployment is from target, we’re about as close as the Committee has ever been to our goal variables in that respect.	13	1
201412	1295	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	We’re closer than we have been 90 percent of the time since 1960.	13	1
201412	1296	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	There are two caveats to the view that I just outlined.	13	1
201412	1297	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	One is the international situation and the other is inflation.	13	1
201412	1298	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	Concerning the international outlook, many in financial markets have been concerned that slower growth in Europe, Japan, and China bodes ill for the US macroeconomic outlook.	13	1
201412	1299	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	We also saw part of the Tealbook looking at a scenario of weaker foreign growth.	13	1
201412	1300	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	I do not think that the situation as it currently stands is threatening to the United States in a direct sense.	13	1
201412	1301	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	While there is certainly some direct effect on the United States from slower global growth, my sense is that the United States is actually likely to benefit from a lower rate structure globally than would have otherwise occurred and from lower oil and gasoline prices than would have otherwise occurred.	13	1
201412	1302	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	The risk, from the perspective of this Committee, with respect to foreign developments is that weak economic performance abroad morphs into a full-blown financial crisis, most likely in Europe or China, as it did in Europe in 2011 and 2012.	13	1
201412	1303	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	Developments in that direction would have important impacts on US financial markets and likely on US macroeconomic performance.	13	1
201412	1304	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	However, as we sit here today, I do not see this as something that we can predict with much accuracy, and I do not think it is any more likely today than it has been since ECB President Draghi’s “whatever it takes” speech in London in 2012 brought the previous crisis to a conclusion.	13	1
201412	1305	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	Domestic inflation has been running below the Committee’s target, but my current forecast continues to call for inflation returning to target over the medium term.	13	1
201412	1306	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	The fact that inflation is running below target is enough to justify a policy rate that is somewhat lower than normal, but it is not enough to justify a policy rate that remains pinned down at zero.	13	1
201412	1307	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	According to leading New Keynesian theories, the main determinant of actual inflation is inflation expectations, and, in this regard, the steep decline in TIPS breakeven inflation rates is quite disconcerting.	13	1
201412	1308	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	I also learned a lot from President Kocherlakota’s memo on inflation and inflation expectations and inflation risk premiums.	13	1
201412	1309	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	My view is that the Board staff is too quick to dismiss these important market developments on inflation expectations.	13	1
201412	1310	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	The worry for me is not so much that year-over-year PCE inflation remains somewhat low, but rather that the shift in inflation expectations is so severe that actual inflation begins to fall further just at the point when the Committee is trying to take on board the robust developments in the real economy.	13	1
201412	1311	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	This may create a situation in which inflation expectations and actual inflation continue to fall instead of rising back toward target as I expect.	13	1
201412	1312	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	A modern central bank cannot afford to be complacent about inflation expectations that are shifting away from target over periods as long as 5 and 10 years.	13	1
201412	1313	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	This problem is severe enough—the 5-year TIPS breakeven was 115 basis points on Friday—that the Committee needs to be prepared to arrest this trend if necessary.	13	1
201412	1314	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	I will discuss ways to be prepared for this possibility more in my policy remarks tomorrow.	13	1
201412	1315	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201412	1316	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	13	1

201412	1363	2014-12-17	meeting	PLOSSER	Of course, then we had the aberration in the first quarter with the winter, which was negative 2 percent; second quarter of 2014, 4.6 percent; third quarter of 2014, 4.6 percent.	13	1

201412	1368	2014-12-17	meeting	PLOSSER	How much evidence does it take us to believe that policy needs to adjust to that strong growth and become a little less accommodative than zero interest rates?	13	1
201412	1369	2014-12-17	meeting	PLOSSER	Continued labor market strength leads me to forecast the unemployment rate falling to 5.7 percent by the end of this year.	13	1
201412	1370	2014-12-17	meeting	PLOSSER	Next year we will see it continue to fall, although probably at a somewhat slower rate, because we are almost at what we think is the long-term sustainable pace.	13	1
201412	1371	2014-12-17	meeting	PLOSSER	We are very near our unemployment rate range that the Committee has for the sustainable rate in the long term.	13	1
201412	1372	2014-12-17	meeting	PLOSSER	I think we will be at 5.4 percent before the middle of next year, and that will begin slowly shrinking, reaching only 5.3 percent by the end of next year.	13	1
201412	1373	2014-12-17	meeting	PLOSSER	Headline inflation will be somewhat softer over the next couple of quarters, as we all know, reflecting the decline in energy prices.	13	1
201412	1374	2014-12-17	meeting	PLOSSER	But those prices should stabilize, and headline inflation will return to that 1½ to 2 percent range over the second half of next year and, I believe, converge to 2 percent in 2016.	13	1
201412	1375	2014-12-17	meeting	PLOSSER	This Committee correctly looked through the very large oil price increases and the increases in headline inflation that we witnessed in 2011, when headline inflation reached over 3 percent in some months and in some quarters.	13	1
201412	1376	2014-12-17	meeting	PLOSSER	We need to do the same thing here.	13	1
201412	1377	2014-12-17	meeting	PLOSSER	We should not let the change in relative prices and their effects on headline inflation drive us to largely reassess our view of inflation in the longer term.	13	1
201412	1378	2014-12-17	meeting	PLOSSER	Again, as many people have said, as long as inflation expectations remain well anchored—and I believe they are—I’m not going to repeat the evidence that others have offered.	13	1
201412	1379	2014-12-17	meeting	PLOSSER	My own view of appropriate policy is somewhat different from my previous SEP submission.	13	1
201412	1380	2014-12-17	meeting	PLOSSER	I have reduced my long-run neutral rate from 4 to 3.75 percent, which I think is consistent mostly for demographic reasons.	13	1
201412	1381	2014-12-17	meeting	PLOSSER	I have also reduced my policy rate because the rules I follow suggest that inflation is going to get back to 2 percent a little later than I previously thought.	13	1
201412	1382	2014-12-17	meeting	PLOSSER	That is cause for making a more gradual adjustment in my policy rate.	13	1
201412	1383	2014-12-17	meeting	PLOSSER	My path calls for liftoff in the first quarter of next year, with gradual rate hikes reaching an IOER rate of 2 percent, but I guess we don’t use IOER—1.875 percent for the midpoint of the federal funds rate target range, to be more precise, by the end of next year.	13	1
201412	1384	2014-12-17	meeting	PLOSSER	I believe by 2017 we should be at our long-run neutral rate of 3.75 percent.	13	1
201412	1385	2014-12-17	meeting	PLOSSER	I think this path is both feasible and desirable, is gradual, and is measured in its approach.	13	1
201412	1386	2014-12-17	meeting	PLOSSER	However, I continue to be concerned that if we do not begin this process reasonably promptly, we will face a much higher risk of having to raise rates much more quickly and, thus, returning to those old go-stop policies of the past.	13	1
201412	1387	2014-12-17	meeting	PLOSSER	When we do that, we will induce greater, not less, economic and financial instability in the years to come.	13	1
201412	1388	2014-12-17	meeting	PLOSSER	Thus, while the Committee may still believe that June is a reasonable expectation for liftoff, I believe it is very important that we convey in our language and our messaging to the markets that there remains significant probability on liftoff before then, and mostly in the first quarter.	13	1
201412	1389	2014-12-17	meeting	PLOSSER	We may not lift off in the first quarter, but the more we encourage the markets to have zero probability on that event, when the time comes for us to move—if that happens to be earlier than the market expects—then we will probably be faced with having to surprise the market substantially and create more volatility than would indeed be necessary.	13	1

201412	1412	2014-12-17	meeting	GEORGE	Similarly, my staff constructed a measure that offers additional information on the amount of spare capacity in the economy.	13	1
201412	1413	2014-12-17	meeting	GEORGE	It combines four different output gap measures along with fiscal policy information, such as personal current tax and corporate tax receipts, to produce a sort of composite output gap.	13	1
201412	1414	2014-12-17	meeting	GEORGE	This measure shows the current output gap in the range of about 1 percent.	13	1
201412	1415	2014-12-17	meeting	GEORGE	Assuming trend growth of 2 percent, a growth rate of 3 percent over the next year will eliminate the excess capacity in the economy according to this measure.	13	1
201412	1416	2014-12-17	meeting	GEORGE	If labor market conditions continue to evolve at a similar pace of improvement, as we have seen over the past 12 months, the economy looks to be about a year away from full capacity and full employment.	13	1
201412	1417	2014-12-17	meeting	GEORGE	With the labor market approaching a level consistent with sustainable long-run economic growth, upward pressure on wages should begin to emerge.	13	1
201412	1418	2014-12-17	meeting	GEORGE	As the quits rate has increased over the past two years, average wage growth from job switchers has risen from roughly 4.3 percent per quarter in early 2013 to 5.6 percent in the third quarter of this year.	13	1

201412	1421	2014-12-17	meeting	GEORGE	With the quits rates rising and returning to pre-recession levels, I expect to see even greater wage growth for job switchers, and eventually for others, as competitive pressures take hold.	13	1
201412	1422	2014-12-17	meeting	GEORGE	Regarding inflation, I expect in the near term there will be downward pressure on domestic prices exerted by slower global growth and the recent shifts in foreign exchange rates.	13	1

201412	1430	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I plan to discuss my troubling inflation outlook, some evidence from labor markets in support of that outlook, and the credibility risk posed by that outlook.	13	1
201412	1431	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	When I talk about my inflation outlook, I just want to be clear about my monetary policy assumption.	13	1
201412	1432	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	My monetary policy assumption that I’m going to be using for the purpose of these remarks is similar to that in Tealbook A, so liftoff in the second quarter of 2015.	13	1
201412	1433	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	That differs from what I do see as appropriate monetary policy.	13	1
201412	1434	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I’m respondent number 10 in the SEP.	13	1
201412	1435	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Like financial markets, I see the fed funds rate at the end of 2017 as being around 2 percent, and so my path for the fed funds rate is considerably lower than the central tendency of this Committee or as modeled in Tealbook A.	13	1
201412	1436	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	But, for the purposes of these remarks, as I said at the beginning, I’m going to be using the same monetary policy assumption as described in Tealbook A.	13	1
201412	1437	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Under that monetary policy assumption, I see inflation returning to target, but only very gradually, in 2018.	13	1
201412	1438	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think it would be useful for us to spend more time in our conversations to dig into the differences in our outlooks for inflation.	13	1
201412	1439	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I thought it was great that some people were offering very specific forecasts that differed from that in Tealbook A, and I thought that was important because that presumably shapes the differences in our policy outlook as well.	13	1
201412	1440	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Digging into why we have those differences in those inflation outlooks, I think, could be very useful.	13	1
201412	1441	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	For me, a key factor underlying my inflation outlook is that improvements in economic activity are anticipated to put only modest upward pressure on inflation.	13	1
201412	1442	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	So the Phillips curve is relatively flat.	13	1
201412	1443	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In my view, this flatness is broadly consistent with the recent behavior of labor markets both in the Ninth District and in the nation.	13	1
201412	1444	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In terms of the Ninth District, in some ways labor markets are very tight there, and we’ve heard some unemployment rates mentioned.	13	1
201412	1445	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Now let’s talk about some low unemployment.	13	1
201412	1446	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The unemployment rate in the Minneapolis–St Paul metropolitan area, which has a population of about 3 million, was 3.2 percent in October.	13	1
201412	1447	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The unemployment rate in Fargo was 2.2 percent.	13	1
201412	1448	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	It’s hardly surprising, with these kinds of unemployment rates, that we hear widespread reports that firms can’t find desirable workers.	13	1
201412	1449	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	But, despite these labor shortages, we continue to hear relatively few reports of wage pressures.	13	1
201412	1450	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Now, outside of the oil boom area in western North Dakota, our business contacts consistently report wage growth in 2014 of 2 to 3 percent, although the reports are often closer to the top of that range than they were a couple years ago.	13	1
201412	1451	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	These are backward-looking data, obviously, so if we look forward it might be different.	13	1
201412	1452	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	What was most surprising to me, I have to say, is that this general pattern holds true even in Fargo, which I had mentioned earlier has a 2.2 percent unemployment rate.	13	1
201412	1453	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Now, many of you, I’m sure, remember your North Dakota geography, but just in case you don’t [laughter], Fargo is on the eastern edge of North Dakota, and it’s 400 miles from the heart of the oil boom on the western side of the state.	13	1
201412	1454	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	It’s a big state.	13	1
201412	1455	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	So this is on the wage-pressure side, and I think one thing we should be trying to drill in at and trying to get a better understanding of is how those wage pressures translate into pricing pressures.	13	1
201412	1456	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	That’s the next step actually, right?	13	1
201412	1457	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Because our goals are shaped in terms of price inflation.	13	1
201412	1458	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Our business contacts generally do not see themselves as having much power to raise prices.	13	1
201412	1459	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	When they talk about wage increases, they say that they will be absorbing those wage increases by reducing margins.	13	1
201412	1460	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In terms of hard evidence, the latest year-over-year CPI increase in the Twin Cities was less than 2 percent.	13	1
201412	1461	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	This basic story is also playing out in the national economy.	13	1
201412	1462	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We have seen a striking improvement in employment in 2014, and it’s possible to see some signs of compensation pressures emerging in the past few quarters.	13	1
201412	1463	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	But, by and large, the improvement in the labor market activity has been associated with little change in wage and price growth.	13	1
201412	1464	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think this recent national evidence and recent Ninth District evidence are consistent with the flat Phillips curves that underlie the Tealbook’s and my sluggish inflation outlook.	13	1
201412	1465	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Now, of course, inflation has already been below target for over 30 months, and, in my assessment, this projected long stay—something like seven to eight years below 2 percent— creates substantial risk to the credibility of our target.	13	1
201412	1466	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	If I were asked, I, too, would answer as several Presidents answered before me.	13	1
201412	1467	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I do believe that our expectations remain well anchored.	13	1
201412	1468	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	My core fundamental belief is that.	13	1
201412	1469	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I have faith in that.	13	1
201412	1470	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	But, I think there is evidence that suggests that there is some risk to that credibility.	13	1
201412	1471	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The continued decline in market-based measures of longer-term inflation expectations over the intermeeting period suggests that the downside risk to our target may already be materializing.	13	1
201412	1472	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	As the Minneapolis staff and I stressed in the memo we sent in the intermeeting period, we think it’s important not to remove these risk premiums when thinking about these market- based measures.	13	1
201412	1473	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Even if you don’t buy into that story, I think that the decline has to be seen as being a signal that we’re seeing a decline in longer-term inflation expectations themselves.	13	1
201412	1474	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Of course, declines in longer-term inflation expectations would spill back and create further downside risks to inflation itself.	13	1
201412	1475	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I want to stress that this erosion of credibility scenario is still only a risk to my baseline outlook, and I wouldn’t necessarily say that it’s a high probability risk.	13	1
201412	1476	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The problem is that the experience in Japan and the more recent experience in Europe both suggest that it would be very hard for us to respond effectively to this risk if it were to materialize.	13	1
201412	1477	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The Japanese central bank is relying on extensive support from the fiscal authority to be able to respond effectively.	13	1
201412	1478	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think we should not be building that into our tools about how to respond to that scenario.	13	1
201412	1479	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	For that reason it’s a risk that bulks large in my policy thinking, and I’ll say more about that in the next go-round, Madam Chair.	13	1
201412	1480	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	13	1
201412	1481	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	Vice Chairman.	13	1
201412	1482	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201412	1483	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Like many others, I’m more confident about the strength and durability of expansion.	13	1
201412	1484	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	There are several reasons for that.	13	1
201412	1485	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	First, the passage of time is important.	13	1
201412	1486	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Many of the headwinds that have blunted the economy’s momentum in recent years have subsided.	13	1
201412	1487	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	The most obvious is on the fiscal side.	13	1
201412	1488	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	I expect the fiscal impulse in 2015 to be slightly positive when one includes both the federal and state and local government sectors.	13	1
201412	1489	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Another headwind that’s subsiding is credit availability.	13	1
201412	1490	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	I think that’s continuing to improve.	13	1
201412	1491	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Some of this presumably represents the better-capitalized banking system, but some may also be due to improved confidence by lenders in the economic outlook.	13	1
201412	1492	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Second, in assessing consumption, I think, along with many others, the outlook is quite positive.	13	1
201412	1493	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	The real income trend is strengthening, helped by lower energy prices, faster payroll growth, and higher hours worked.	13	1
201412	1494	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Interesting to me, the New York Fed’s most recent Survey of Consumer Expectations, which was released last week, shows a meaningful uptick in household one-year-ahead expectations for both nominal earnings growth and nominal household income.	13	1
201412	1495	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Translate that to real, and it’s an even bigger uptick.	13	1
201412	1496	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Third, lower oil prices I view as likely to be a substantial positive for global growth.	13	1
201412	1497	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	In particular, the lower headline inflation is already provoking a more-aggressive monetary policy response in Europe and Japan, and, more importantly, the drop in oil prices should lead to a shift in the global fiscal stance toward stimulus as oil exporters faced with much lower oil income run smaller surpluses and/or bigger deficits.	13	1
201412	1498	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	On the other side, for some oil importers, the drop in energy prices represents a very large windfall.	13	1
201412	1499	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	This is a huge transfer from oil producers to importers.	13	1
201412	1500	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	A $40 drop in the per barrel price of oil represents a transfer of about $1 trillion a year from oil producers to oil importers, which I think is significant.	13	1
201412	1501	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	In terms of the inflation outlook, I’m not very worried about the fact that lower oil prices are pushing down the headline inflation rate.	13	1
201412	1502	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	The effect is likely to be temporary as long as it doesn’t affect wage trends or inflationary expectations, and I would say those conditions are broadly satisfied at this point.	13	1
201412	1503	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	With respect to survey measures of inflation expectations, it’s true that the November University of Michigan survey dipped, but we saw a partial retracement of that in the December preliminary results.	13	1
201412	1504	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Moreover, I think the decline that we saw in the November Michigan survey is not really corroborated by other surveys of household inflation expectations.	13	1
201412	1505	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	For example, the New York Fed survey shows expectations at both the one-year and three-year horizons as having been stable recently.	13	1
201412	1506	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	I asked my staff, “How should I reconcile the differences between the University of Michigan results and the New York Fed survey, and what should I put more weight on?”	13	1
201412	1507	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	What do you think the answer was?	13	1
201412	1508	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	I don’t think this reflects bias [laughter] in the particular measurement.	13	1
201412	1509	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	I think there’s a pretty strong case to be made that the New York Fed survey is actually the superior measure.	13	1
201412	1510	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	A few key points worth mentioning.	13	1
201412	1511	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	The first point is that the University of Michigan inflation expectations survey is much more sensitive to oil and gasoline price developments than the New York Fed survey.	13	1
201412	1512	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	This may be due to the fact that the University of Michigan survey asks about prices, which brings gasoline prices into people’s minds, while the New York Fed survey asks the question in terms of inflation.	13	1
201412	1513	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	The second point is when oil and gas prices drop, it’s quite common that this actually feeds through to 5-to-10- year-forward inflation expectations in the University of Michigan survey.	13	1
201412	1514	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	In other words, what we’re seeing in terms of the University of Michigan survey right now—a big drop in oil prices and that leading to a drop in 5-to-10-year-forward inflation expectations—is not unusual.	13	1
201412	1515	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	It’s actually pretty typical, and that means, I think, we should discount it more heavily.	13	1
201412	1516	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	The last point is that there seems to be quite a bit more noise in the University of Michigan survey compared with the New York Fed survey in terms of measurement error.	13	1
201412	1517	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	The sample for the New York Fed survey is considerably larger, and, more importantly, it’s panel data.	13	1
201412	1518	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	We’re asking the same people the same question month after month.	13	1
201412	1519	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	I think the New York Fed survey appears to be the more reliable measure.	13	1
201412	1520	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	With respect to wages, which is sort of the second parameter that might cause you to become more worried about inflation expectations, the trend doesn’t seem to have changed much.	13	1
201412	1521	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	In particular, there’s no evidence that nominal wage growth is declining.	13	1
201412	1522	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	In fact, if you look really closely at the recent ECI and average hourly earnings data, if anything, wage compensation trends may be starting to firm just a little bit.	13	1
201412	1523	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	When I look at the survey-based measures of inflation expectations, when I look at nominal wage growth, both of those series suggest that we should look through the effect of the oil price decline on overall inflation.	13	1
201412	1524	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	With nominal incomes rising at more than a 4 percent annual rate and the risk of recession very low, it seems that the risk of the type of debt deflation dynamic for the United States is very low right now, and that’s very different than the situation in Europe and Japan, in which both inflation and nominal income growth are much lower.	13	1
201412	1525	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	In fact, when I review the inflation statistics, as I raised in the question to the staff earlier, I’m a bit surprised that the core deflator has remained stuck at 1½ percent.	13	1
201412	1526	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	I was actually thinking that it would decline a bit because of the decline in energy prices and the appreciation of the dollar.	13	1
201412	1527	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Now, in many ways, although we’re wringing our hands and worrying that inflation is below our target, in some ways it’s actually a good thing.	13	1
201412	1528	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	It does allow us to be more patient in terms of the timing of liftoff, and it also should enable us to probe more aggressively to see how low full employment actually is as we go through the monetary policy normalization process.	13	1
201412	1529	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	If inflation was running at 2.3 percent or 2.4 percent today, we’d be having a very different conversation.	13	1
201412	1530	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	I think we’re going to want to let the unemployment rate fall slightly below its natural rate in order to push inflation up, and that has a pretty significant benefit.	13	1
201412	1531	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	That tight labor market should create pressure to rehire some of the long-term unemployed, which would be good not just for them, but good for the country because it would expand the economy’s productive capacity.	13	1
201412	1532	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Finally, in terms of risks to the outlook, I think they really seem to lie mostly overseas at this point.	13	1
201412	1533	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	One risk we haven’t talked about in any detail is the recent developments in Russia.	13	1
201412	1534	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	The ruble has declined precipitously.	13	1
201412	1535	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	That’s caused the Russian central bank to raise interest rates substantially, and it’s not really clear that they’re in a position that’s going to turn out to be sustainable.	13	1
201412	1536	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	This, of course, would ripple back mostly to Europe if you think about what the near-term effects would be, through the trade channel and also through their banking system exposures.	13	1
201412	1537	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Several large European banks have significant exposure to Russian corporates on the order of 50 percent or more of their core Tier 1 capital.	13	1
201412	1538	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	I also think the developments in Russia are also concerning from a geopolitical basis.	13	1
201412	1539	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	I would think that as the economic circumstances of Russia deteriorate, Vladimir Putin will have an incentive to take greater risks geopolitically to divert attention from what’s an increasingly problematic domestic economy.	13	1

201412	1549	2014-12-17	meeting	FISCHER	It tends to come down.	13	1

201412	1557	2014-12-17	meeting	FISCHER	First, investment will be reduced by the decline in energy investment.	13	1

201412	1560	2014-12-17	meeting	FISCHER	Here I take some encouragement from the fact that the staff forecasts increases in foreign growth, particularly in Europe, in the coming years, and one really hopes that is right for many reasons.	13	1

201412	1562	2014-12-17	meeting	FISCHER	But the Tealbook does not believe that will happen, and I take some comfort from that.	13	1
201412	1563	2014-12-17	meeting	FISCHER	Further, and here Vice Chairman Dudley and I have not spoken previously, we do not know how the volatility in the price of oil and the associated financial market instability will affect the world economy, nor do we know what the geopolitical consequences of the unfolding Russian economic crisis, which is becoming very difficult for the Russians, will be.	13	1
201412	1564	2014-12-17	meeting	FISCHER	In short, although this feels much better, we do have to remind ourselves that two or three quarters of good data do not establish a solid trend.	13	1
201412	1565	2014-12-17	meeting	FISCHER	We have several times hoped we were heading back to 3 percent growth only to have to reduce our forecasts in light of weaker data.	13	1
201412	1566	2014-12-17	meeting	FISCHER	That is also to say that we have always to remind ourselves that our forecasts have very wide, not narrow, confidence bands around them.	13	1
201412	1567	2014-12-17	meeting	FISCHER	Despite the headwinds I have just noted, I am, on balance, also relatively optimistic about the prospects for both the labor markets and overall growth.	13	1

201412	1572	2014-12-17	meeting	FISCHER	As the Chair has said, the FOMC has looked through the higher price of oil on several previous occasions, including notably in 2008.	13	1
201412	1573	2014-12-17	meeting	FISCHER	The FOMC was right to do that then, and we will be similarly right to look through the lower price of oil now.	13	1
201412	1574	2014-12-17	meeting	FISCHER	I expect we will all agree that this is the right approach, in particular because the extremely low inflation expected in the next year or so is the result of a positive supply shock, which is growth-inducing, rather than the result of exceptionally low demand, which is the fear behind very low inflation when you are thinking of temporary inflation.	13	1
201412	1575	2014-12-17	meeting	FISCHER	The more serious inflation problem is to be found in the Tealbook forecast for core inflation for the coming years—2014 and 2015 have core inflation of 1½ percent, which is obviously significantly below our 2 percent target—and the Tealbook predicts that even by 2017 the core inflation rate will be 1.8 percent and not yet 2 percent.	13	1
201412	1576	2014-12-17	meeting	FISCHER	Well, how should we think about this core inflation?	13	1
201412	1577	2014-12-17	meeting	FISCHER	I have two main reactions.	13	1
201412	1578	2014-12-17	meeting	FISCHER	The first is to point out that 1.8 percent is very close to 2 percent.	13	1
201412	1579	2014-12-17	meeting	FISCHER	Using the staff’s baseline prediction for inflation, and estimating probabilities using stochastic simulations of the FRB/US model kindly supplied by the staff, the probability that inflation in 2017 will be greater than 2 percent is 40 percent, and above 1.8 percent is 48 percent.	13	1
201412	1580	2014-12-17	meeting	FISCHER	We are not talking about very different outcomes for inflation.	13	1
201412	1581	2014-12-17	meeting	FISCHER	My second reaction is to say that while I believe the staff’s views as reflected in the Tealbook forecast are plausible, there are several possible reasons to expect, nonetheless, that nominal wage growth may begin to rise more than predicted in the Tealbook as the level of unemployment continues to decline.	13	1
201412	1582	2014-12-17	meeting	FISCHER	One reason is the basic economics of supply and demand.	13	1
201412	1583	2014-12-17	meeting	FISCHER	That is, of course, taken into account in the Tealbook, because there are increases in price inflation and nominal wage growth in the Tealbook forecast.	13	1
201412	1584	2014-12-17	meeting	FISCHER	But I would add to that a lesson of experience that when one proclaims the end of a well-established relationship, more often than not, that is the moment that the relationship makes its presence known shortly thereafter.	13	1
201412	1585	2014-12-17	meeting	FISCHER	I think this may well happen again in the case of the flat Phillips curve.	13	1
201412	1586	2014-12-17	meeting	FISCHER	Let’s go back to the key question, which is, what should we do?	13	1
