201412	1596	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	I join the general view that has been expressed this afternoon that the steady growth of what is almost now a year’s duration is likely to continue.	13	1
201412	1597	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	Like President Lacker and a few others here, I found myself looking for reasons to believe that this time, the relatively strong performance will continue, as opposed to our past pattern of a period of sustained decent growth faltering after fiscal or monetary stimulus has been removed.	13	1
201412	1598	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	Several of you have mentioned some reasons to believe that.	13	1
201412	1599	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	I will just note three quickly.	13	1
201412	1600	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	One, I just alluded to the fact that, this time around, when we began tapering early this year and through the end of the LSAPs,, we didn’t see the kind of stumbles that occurred earlier when either fiscal or monetary stimulus was withdrawn, and what had been a promising period of an uptick in growth was followed by a disappointing couple of quarters.	13	1
201412	1601	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	Two, as Jeff also noted, beyond the continued improvement in the unemployment rate and the recent strength of monthly jobs numbers, we are now seeing more structural dynamism in labor markets.	13	1
201412	1602	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	Following on the increases in job openings, albeit with some lag, the quits rate has been edging up this year.	13	1
201412	1603	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	It is now solidly in pre-crisis territory, which is probably notable since each of the past two recessions resulted in the quits rate never quite getting back to where it had been previously.	13	1
201412	1604	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	That is some indication of an uptick in dynamism.	13	1
201412	1605	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	The hires rate isn’t quite there yet, but it has also improved, on net, this year.	13	1
201412	1606	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	Three, while it is hard to say where the equilibrium point for household debt is or should be, it is pretty clear that a considerable amount of deleveraging has taken place.	13	1
201412	1607	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	We are now at levels of household debt comparable with those prevailing in the early years of the past decade, before the effect of the mortgage mania had accelerated the growth of household debt.	13	1
201412	1608	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	The pace of decline in the ratio of household debt to GDP has diminished considerably in the past year or so.	13	1
201412	1609	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	It is not unreasonable to think that the change in the second derivative will portend some leveling off of this ratio in the not-too-distant future, an inference that is buttressed by the fact that the dollar amount of total household debt has risen modestly over the past year.	13	1
201412	1610	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	I should probably add that student debt accounts for a fair bit of that increase, and serious delinquency rates of student debt have risen quite a bit, now surpassing credit card debt, which was the traditional leader in this category.	13	1
201412	1611	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	This is hardly an unalloyed good.	13	1
201412	1612	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	Now, as Governor Fischer and President Lockhart have already said, and I think Jay may say it as well, it is not as though we have unqualifiedly good news.	13	1
201412	1613	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	But I think that what we have seen explains and justifies the prevailing attitude today that, with continued progress for another couple of quarters, concerns about premature liftoff or the inevitable choppiness of the first rate increase will diminish enough to put a federal funds rate increase in play.	13	1
201412	1614	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	On the other hand, as Governor Fischer also pointed out, there is a considerable amount of uncertainty that remains.	13	1
201412	1615	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	On the upside of economic performance, it is possible that we would get unexpectedly high jobs numbers for the next few months, along with more concrete signs of accelerating wage increases.	13	1
201412	1616	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	I’m sure that would lead some to want to consider an earlier liftoff.	13	1
201412	1617	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	From my perspective, there are at least two plausible scenarios that would make me, at least, more hesitant to move in the June–September timeframe that is represented by many of the dots of voters in this SEP.	13	1
201412	1618	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	One, which has already been mentioned by several people, is the external downside risk from global markets.	13	1
201412	1619	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	It is certainly reasonable to expect, as the Tealbook does, that the euro zone will improve slightly next year, and that some form of QE there will help stave off any deflationary or recession threat.	13	1
201412	1620	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	But the euro zone does lack much capacity to absorb any further shocks, whether from renewed sovereign debt problems or geopolitical turmoil or other sources.	13	1
201412	1621	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	Were things to go awry in the euro zone and China’s growth to slow more than the current consensus suggests, financial markets, and market psychology more generally, might pose risks to the United States.	13	1
201412	1622	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	I know that most models suggest a limited vulnerability to external developments of this sort, but my memory, at least, of past episodes suggests that the models may be missing something, particularly in the absence of either fiscal or monetary stimulus in the United States.	13	1
201412	1623	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	I think Governor Brainard, fortunately, probably has a better perspective on this than I.	13	1
201412	1624	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	The other scenario is the one that concerns me perhaps more, and that’s anticipating that jobs numbers and other indicators, including unemployment, may suggest, by the first part of next year, continued moderate strengthening of labor markets, but that there also would be evidence of labor participation increasing, part-time employment diminishing, and still no real signs of wage acceleration, much less upward pressure on inflation.	13	1
201412	1625	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	The question would be what to do in those circumstances.	13	1
201412	1626	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	This returns me to a theme that I’ve sounded, probably ad nauseum, over the past year or two here, which is that with all of the uncertainties in labor markets, we all have to admit that we have been surprised about something that has happened in labor markets over the past couple of years, and we are well advised to be pretty pragmatic and pretty data sensitive in thinking about and assessing what is actually going on in labor markets.	13	1
201412	1627	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	There are some labor economists who are already beginning to do some work on what they find to be the changes in life-cycle labor market behavior that could conceivably be second only to the broad entry into the labor market of women over a three-decade period in changing the shape of labor market behavior.	13	1
201412	1628	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	We don’t know whether that is actually occurring yet, but we do know that a lot of things that have happened in labor markets—participation rates and other things—haven’t conformed to what might have been expected based on pre-crisis behavior.	13	1
201412	1629	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	This may be another area in which the crisis and the Great Recession have accelerated trends that were previously a little harder to detect.	13	1
201412	1630	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	When we look at wages and the anticipation of wage increases, even though the NFIB is now predicting more wage increases being paid by its members—we should probably note that they have been predicting that for two years now, and we haven’t yet seen it realized.	13	1
201412	1631	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	As I think Presidents Kocherlakota and Rosengren have both pointed out, in some discrete analyses that their staffs did, there is some reason to believe that the performance of labor markets and wage markets in the past is not necessarily a great predictor of where we are right now.	13	1
201412	1632	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	Then Governor Fischer alluded to the Phillips-curve issue, and that the slope may indeed change or revert to where it has been.	13	1
201412	1633	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	But for a while now, the Phillips curve has been pretty flat, and we can’t predict with any certainty that it will normalize, understanding that “normal” may vary from time to time.	13	1
201412	1634	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	Again, this all leads me to the anticipation that if we face this set of circumstances in the spring or the early summer, I think it behooves us to think carefully about whether we would be prepared to lift off, notwithstanding the fact that there will have been continued economic growth in that period.	13	1
201412	1635	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	I don’t know that that’s where we’ll be.	13	1
201412	1636	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	I actually think it’s not so likely that we will have six more months of really solid job numbers and not see some changes in wage patterns and part-time unemployment, but we might, and I think we should just remain open to that.	13	1
201412	1637	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	What we’ve been doing in the past couple of meetings, I think, is trying to begin weaning the markets gradually off what has been something like calendar-based guidance and more toward a focus on conditions as we see them evolving in the nearer term.	13	1
201412	1638	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	I just want us to make sure that we don’t replace a calendar approach for holding off rate increases with a calendar approach for starting them and instead really stick to what we all tend to mouth as the mantra— that we want to be reacting to conditions, be state contingent, be conditional, whatever one’s favorite phrase is—and that, I continue to think, will probably serve us best over the next couple of quarters.	13	1
201412	1639	2014-12-17	meeting	TARULLO	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201412	1640	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	13	1
201412	1641	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Powell.	13	1
201412	1642	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201412	1643	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	My forecast is very close to that of the December Tealbook and, for that matter, the September Tealbook.	13	1
201412	1644	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	I see continued growth in the region of 2½ percent.	13	1
201412	1645	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	Consumer spending ought to be strong, supported by much lower energy prices, higher levels of confidence, continued low interest rates, and higher stock prices.	13	1
201412	1646	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	Businesses should respond by hiring and investing.	13	1
201412	1647	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	In the labor market I see continued improvement across a broad range of measures, including strong payroll growth at well over 200,000 per month, a flattening out of labor force participation at roughly current levels for a couple of years at least, and the elimination of remaining slack.	13	1
201412	1648	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	Wages ought to react positively.	13	1
201412	1649	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	In fact, we may already be seeing the beginning of that, and I see inflation moving back up to the 2 percent objective as slack is eliminated.	13	1
201412	1650	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	The one place where I differ very modestly from the baseline is in the pace of rate increases.	13	1
201412	1651	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	In particular, it seems to me that if we are broadly on the baseline path, we would be raising rates more than 25 basis points per quarter in 2016, and that’s what the baseline shows.	13	1
201412	1652	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	I would think we would be moving along a little more rapidly than that, but it’s not a huge difference.	13	1
201412	1653	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	Also, I would say I take some positive signal from the Reserve Bank inquiries of District business contacts.	13	1
201412	1654	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	It’s nice to see measures like that coming up all over the place that tend to suggest that the time for wage increases and greater hiring is coming soon.	13	1
201412	1655	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	I find this narrative, which is broadly that of the Tealbook and the central tendency of the SEP, both fairly plausible and fairly positive.	13	1
201412	1656	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	In fact, I would go so far as to say there’s real upside.	13	1
201412	1657	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	I don’t think anyone should fall over dead with surprise if the alternative view on pages 6 and 7 of Tealbook A, materializes since all it does is represent a straight-lining, in effect, of 2014.	13	1
201412	1658	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	That said, in the spirit of poking holes in this consensus and perhaps the spirit of cautious contrarianism, I think Dennis said, I’m going to mention three gaps or disconnects and also one emerging risk scenario that I think could threaten the narrative.	13	1
201412	1659	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	And I have to admit, I can’t dismiss them from my mind, and we’ve talked about these in one form or another.	13	1
201412	1660	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	The first is the gap between the relatively strong performance here in the United States and the weakness we see in Europe and elsewhere around the world, the threat being that we will feel this weakness over time, perhaps through the stronger dollar or through the risk-off channel if the bad events do happen.	13	1
201412	1661	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	I see this as the principal threat to the baseline narrative.	13	1
201412	1662	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	The alternative scenario in Tealbook A, titled “Weaker Foreign Growth and Stronger Dollar,” captures that pretty well.	13	1
201412	1663	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	The second gap is one we spent some time on today, and that is the gap between survey measures of inflation expectations, which are stable, and market-based inflation compensation based on TIPS and inflation swaps, which show meaningful declines at the distant horizon.	13	1
201412	1664	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	I thought that the paper that Yuriy Kitsul shared before the meeting was quite useful, showing that inflation compensation between 5 and 10 years out has declined by 72 basis points so far this year—it’s actually more than that now, this is a week-old paper.	13	1
201412	1665	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	And different models propose different decompositions of this change, as we’ve discussed.	13	1
201412	1666	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	The Board model happens to assign the smallest amount to actual expectations of lower inflation and to inflation risk premiums and the largest amount to liquidity premiums, which is really meant to capture the greater attraction of nominals due to their higher liquidity as well as other factors related to supply and demand.	13	1
201412	1667	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	Other models tend to agree that there’s relatively little to be seen in actual changes in inflation expectations but assign greater increases to the inflation risk premium.	13	1
201412	1668	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	Inflation swaps send a similar signal.	13	1
201412	1669	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	I look at all of these, and my instinct is to dismiss them and want to go with the survey-based measures, but I have to admit they raise concerns.	13	1
201412	1670	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	It’s very difficult to convince oneself that there isn’t something here to at least be concerned about, and it will bear close monitoring.	13	1
201412	1671	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	The third gap I will mention is that between the median rate forecast in the SEP and the baseline, on the one hand, and the forecast reflected in market readings, on the other hand—and that gap is now quite large.	13	1
201412	1672	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	At the short end, OIS quotes show a rate of about 1½ percent at year-end 2016 compared with about 2½ percent in the SEP.	13	1
201412	1673	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	Some of that may reflect a difference between the Committee’s modal outlook and the risk-neutral pricing of OIS, but not all of it.	13	1
201412	1674	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	At the longer end, if you drop the SEP forecast and pretend it’s a 10-year bond, you get a yield to maturity of about 3 percent, but the yield this morning was about 2.07 percent, and the difference is that the Treasury market is pricing in a much lower path of rates.	13	1
201412	1675	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	The one-year- forward rate in five years is 2.7 percent, fully 100 basis points below the Committee’s long-run equilibrium.	13	1
201412	1676	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	Why is the market pricing in lower yields than the Committee?	13	1
201412	1677	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	Board models attribute about half of that to term premiums and only small amounts to real short rates and expected inflation.	13	1
201412	1678	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	I guess there are two narratives.	13	1
201412	1679	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	One may be that the market is concerned about the possibility of weaker growth and lower expected inflation.	13	1
201412	1680	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	Another explanation is that, given the sharp differences in economic performance and expectations for policy, global fixed income investors would rather own dollar-denominated risk-free instruments at the 10-year tenor yielding 2 percent rather than other alternatives like comparable euro-denominated instruments that yield 0.6 percent or even lower-yielding Japanese ones.	13	1
201412	1681	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	The recent data tend to support this story.	13	1
201412	1682	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	My own sense is that the Treasury market is, in fact, pricing in lower oil prices and stronger foreign demand for Treasuries as opposed to concerns about slower US growth or lower inflation.	13	1
201412	1683	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	But there is likely some truth in both these explanations.	13	1
201412	1684	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	Again, I find it hard to dismiss that.	13	1
201412	1685	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	Separately, I would add another risk scenario, which is certainly not an odds-on thing at this point, but I think there may be a heightened risk of an emerging markets selloff or even a rout driven by declining oil prices, a stronger dollar, and evolving events in Russia.	13	1
201412	1686	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	The sensitivity of investors to these developments may be tested by the likely acknowledgement in tomorrow’s statement that the time for increases in US interest rates may be drawing near.	13	1
201412	1687	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	In any case, these three gaps will be adjusted or eliminated over time.	13	1
201412	1688	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	I’m not suggesting that that process needs to be destabilizing or destructive, but I do think that they point to risks of weaker growth and lower inflation, and perhaps I’m just constitutionally more focused on avoiding downside risks, or it may be that the risks to the downside actually are greater and represent more difficult challenges for policy than the upside risks—for example, the risk that we might get several more payroll reports well in the 300,000 level.	13	1
201412	1689	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	I’ll have more to say on that tomorrow.	13	1

201412	1693	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Since we last met, we’ve had two strong payroll reports, and American consumers are demonstrating more confidence both in their actions and in their expectations, bolstered, in part, by significantly lower prices at the pump.	13	1
201412	1694	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	These are very welcome developments.	13	1
201412	1695	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	But we also see the increasingly resilient growth in the United States taking place against a backdrop of considerable risks to the outlook in several important foreign economies, and the dollar has continued its sharp appreciation.	13	1
201412	1696	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	In addition, progress in moving inflation back up toward our target has been quite limited, even looking through the recent sharp drop in oil prices.	13	1
201412	1697	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	On balance, then, I would say that conditions continue to validate our strategy of ending asset purchases in October—this time for real, or so we hope—while remaining somewhat patient on the removal of monetary accommodation, even as we see the day of liftoff coming, I think, into clearer view.	13	1
201412	1698	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	The news from the labor market has been unambiguously positive.	13	1
201412	1699	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	The unemployment rate has moved down further.	13	1
201412	1700	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Payroll employment is now averaging above 280,000 per month.	13	1
201412	1701	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	And whereas previously nearly all of the take-up in slack was seen only in the overall unemployment rate, now we’re seeing other margins of slack also showing improvement.	13	1
201412	1702	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	The participation rate has been about flat since the spring, which is encouraging, given that we think there is an underlying trend of decline, and it suggests some cyclical improvement.	13	1
201412	1703	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	The number of employees working part time for economic reasons has moved noticeably lower in the past three months after remaining stubbornly high, and it’s also notable that most of the reduction in unemployment over the past year has been accounted for by a welcome and overdue reduction in long-term unemployment.	13	1
201412	1704	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	But, of course, while we see evidence that labor market slack is diminishing across a number of dimensions, we don’t actually have very good measurements of how much slack remains.	13	1
201412	1705	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Moreover, we see no clear evidence of a broad-based acceleration in wages.	13	1
201412	1706	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	We hear a lot of anecdotes.	13	1
201412	1707	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	There are some regional and skill-specific pressures, but all three of the measures that we traditionally look at on the aggregate measure of wages show increases from a year ago that are still mired in the 2 to 2¼ percent range, well below increases prior to the crisis and little different from the pace in recent years.	13	1
201412	1708	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	The incoming data on aggregate spending, I think, reinforce the picture of solid underlying growth momentum in the domestic economy.	13	1
201412	1709	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	The data on consumer spending received after publication of the Tealbook suggest that second-half GDP is increasing at above a 3 percent pace, which is very welcome.	13	1
201412	1710	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	The continued low rates and the recent sharp declines in oil prices should continue to boost consumer spending into the next year, while also, on balance, providing a plus to business investment and output.	13	1
201412	1711	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	It’s also significant that potential disruptions to the fiscal-policy trajectory, which have damaged incipient recoveries previously, have been taken off the table, which removes a significant source of risk.	13	1
201412	1712	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	One note of weakness, I think, on the domestic aggregate demand front is familiar.	13	1
201412	1713	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	We still see weakness in single-family housing, and the data that we saw this morning has single- family permits, the best gauge of activity in this sector, changing little again.	13	1
201412	1714	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Now, on the risk side, I think the inflation picture bears continued vigilance.	13	1
201412	1715	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Even looking through the recent sharp declines in oil prices on the assumption they will stabilize and pass through to retail prices over the next two quarters, the level of inflation that might be expected to prevail seems to be centered around 1½ percent, below our target.	13	1
201412	1716	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Although there are good reasons to expect inflation to move up toward the target as slack is eliminated, we haven’t seen any sustained movement in that direction thus far.	13	1
201412	1717	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Taken together with the recent shift down in market-based indications of inflation expectations, this points to some downside risks in the inflation outlook, especially given the backdrop of falling commodity prices and disinflationary pressures abroad.	13	1
201412	1718	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	We also are seeing some financial risks from the big adjustments recently in the price of oil, and they bear watching, I think.	13	1
201412	1719	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	It’s also important to recognize possible risks from a further deterioration in economic conditions abroad.	13	1
201412	1720	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	The intermeeting period saw further evidence of stagnation or weakening in economic activity in some of the largest foreign economies, further monetary accommodation or expectations of future easing in response, and a further notable increase in the dollar.	13	1
201412	1721	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Realized and expected changes in foreign monetary policy arise in the context of continued underperformance in key foreign economies struggling with deflationary pressures, compounded in some cases by an unwillingness or inability to engage in meaningful fiscal support to domestic demand and ongoing and unresolved structural challenges.	13	1
201412	1722	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Recent events in Greece remind us that although there has been notable progress, threats to financial stability in the euro area remain.	13	1
201412	1723	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Although the United States obviously has a very large and diversified internal market, this doesn’t imply that we are in any way a closed economy or immune from foreign shocks.	13	1
201412	1724	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Connections between the United States and foreign markets are still extremely large in both directions, and recent experience tells us that financial market disturbances abroad can have very large effects on US asset prices and on financial markets more generally.	13	1
201412	1725	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Due to the lag in the dollar’s effects on trade, net exports will likely continue to subtract from GDP growth over the medium term.	13	1
201412	1726	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Moreover, I suspect that increases in the value of the dollar have not yet run their course.	13	1
201412	1727	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Staff memos have noted that, on net, the effect of dollar appreciation on US GDP growth can be expected to be relatively modest, but this net effect conceals two important and significant gross effects, an initial and substantial depressing effect of dollar increases on net exports and a subsequent, partially offsetting positive effect from a more-accommodative monetary policy.	13	1
201412	1728	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	If a strengthening dollar does weigh heavily on net exports, all else being equal, we will need to adjust the pace of normalization in response.	13	1
201412	1729	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	The good news is that the US economy and financial system have become more resilient over the past two years, and internal sources of demand seem sufficiently strong, particularly with the boost from low gas prices, to continue growth momentum in the face of headwinds from abroad.	13	1
201412	1730	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	But I would not lightly dismiss risks that those headwinds could intensify.	13	1
201412	1731	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Overall, when considering appropriate policy, I would place robust domestic demand growth in the context of a global environment of weak foreign aggregate demand and large persistent disinflationary pressures.	13	1
201412	1732	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Such an environment, in my view, suggests that downside risks to US growth remain, and, coupled with persistently weak core inflation below our target and some deterioration in measures of inflation expectations, it warrants a still cautious approach to policy normalization.	13	1
201412	1733	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1

201412	1759	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	Looking at your SEP submissions and some of your comments, the growth outlook beyond this year hasn’t actually changed much since September, but most of you are anticipating above-trend growth.	13	1
201412	1760	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	We’ve been disappointed before, and President Lockhart and others remind us that we should be careful not to become overconfident, but I did hear a good deal of upbeat sentiment around the table that you think the economy really is exhibiting greater momentum.	13	1
201412	1761	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	You feel increased confidence that next year will be a year in which we do see a faster pace of growth, and that the expansion seems to be on track.	13	1
201412	1762	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	The continued decline in oil prices since our October meeting is one of the most notable economic developments shaping the outlook.	13	1
201412	1763	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	Many of you noted that the spending stimulus due to lower energy prices does provide an offset to the restraint from the stronger dollar, and consumers, especially low-income consumers, should benefit from the decline in energy prices.	13	1
201412	1764	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	We had an interesting discussion about the likely impact of lower energy prices on North American drilling activity and capital spending, and that’s something that will bear close watching.	13	1
201412	1765	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	But I think all of you agreed that, on balance, the net effect of the decline in oil prices for US GDP growth is positive—at least of the magnitude of decline we’ve seen so far.	13	1
201412	1766	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	However, some of you noted the effect that the decline in oil prices will have on the global economy.	13	1
201412	1767	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	Even though one can make the case that the net effect is positive, there really are very different regional effects, taking account of the possibility in Europe of pushing inflation expectations down and financial market effects.	13	1
201412	1768	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	This is something that’s going to bear close watching and is a risk.	13	1
201412	1769	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	With respect to the US outlook, a number of you also pointed to increased consumer confidence and expressed your belief that a good dynamic, a kind of self-reinforcing multiplier- accelerator type of positive dynamic, may finally be coming into play.	13	1
201412	1770	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	Turning to inflation, incoming data during the intermeeting period have been mixed.	13	1
201412	1771	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	Tealbook revised up its estimate of core PCE inflation in the current quarter after seeing October’s data.	13	1
201412	1772	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	Tomorrow morning we’ll look at the CPI release and see if that’s consistent with this assessment.	13	1
201412	1773	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	On the other hand, though, the drag from declining energy prices on headline inflation now looks like it will be larger than previously projected, with the 12-month rate likely to drop below 1 percent early next year.	13	1
201412	1774	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	Moreover, several of you pointed to downward pressure on inflation from dollar appreciation, which likely will lower non-energy commodity and imported goods prices.	13	1
201412	1775	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	On the question of whether lower energy prices and the higher dollar will leave an imprint on inflation beyond the next couple of quarters, I heard mixed views.	13	1
201412	1776	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	A number of you expressed confidence in your projection that inflation will likely move back to 2 percent over time in an environment of continued improvement in the labor market.	13	1
201412	1777	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	A number of you pointed out that, with respect to inflation expectations, survey-based measures have remained stable and suggest that long-run inflation expectations are well anchored.	13	1
201412	1778	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	And we’ve had a very rich discussion that I’m not even going to try to summarize regarding how to interpret the decline we’ve seen in five-year, five-year-forward breakevens that have continued to decline further since our October meeting.	13	1
201412	1779	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	The staff’s financial Board briefing yesterday pointed out that there are an awful lot of different ways to break this down into inflation expectations, inflation risk premiums, and liquidity effects, and the breakdown that one gets is actually highly model sensitive.	13	1
201412	1780	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	I think this is something, obviously, to which we’re going to be paying close attention as we go forward.	13	1
201412	1781	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	All in all, while most of you see the drop in headline inflation as largely transitory and continue to expect that it will move gradually back toward 2 percent, some of you are concerned that we may be seeing the beginning of a worrisome downward adjustment in inflation expectations.	13	1
201412	1782	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	If inflation expectations were to shift down markedly, this would create downside risks to inflation itself, and a failure on our part to take decisive action could exacerbate this risk by diminishing the credibility of our commitment to our 2 percent inflation objective.	13	1
201412	1783	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	Clearly, inflation developments will bear close watching.	13	1
201412	1784	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	Let me stop there and see if anyone would like to comment on this summary.	13	1
201412	1785	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	[No response]	13	1
201412	1786	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	Okay.	13	1
201412	1787	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	Then let me just add a few brief comments of my own.	13	1
201412	1788	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	First, I want to join with the others who described incoming news pertaining to the labor market as encouraging.	13	1
201412	1789	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	My own reaction to incoming data, including the two employment reports, is that we are seeing a pattern of across-the-board improvement in labor market conditions.	13	1
201412	1790	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	Virtually every indicator I monitor shows movement in the right direction.	13	1
201412	1791	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	For example, I consider the quits rate a very useful cyclical indicator, and I’m encouraged by the increase we have seen in the past couple of reports.	13	1
201412	1792	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	A substantial share of quits results from job offers that employed workers receive and accept, and an increase in the prevalence of such offers points to the possibility of more-rapid wage increases and, I think, suggests real improvement in the labor market.	13	1
201412	1793	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	To the extent that there are also people who quit into unemployment, an increase in these flows suggests that workers have become less wary about leaving one job without having lined up the next.	13	1
201412	1794	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	I’m similarly encouraged by the more favorable assessments of the labor market we’re seeing in household surveys.	13	1
201412	1795	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	If you will forgive me for returning yet again to my cross- country road trip analogy [laughter], whereas in October my assessment was that we were just pulling into Cleveland, by now I think we’ve left President Mester’s office.	13	1
201412	1796	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	We’re in the process of crossing the Allegheny Mountains.	13	1
201412	1797	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	There remains some way to go to the Weehawkin end of the Lincoln Tunnel, but I’m feeling a lot more hopeful now that we’ll make it all the way to Manhattan without hitting any major delay.	13	1
201412	1798	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	Let me turn to inflation.	13	1
201412	1799	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	Due to the recent momentum we have seen in the labor market, coupled with the downward pressure we are seeing on inflation, it now seems likely that the economy will return to maximum employment before inflation is returned to our 2 percent objective.	13	1
201412	1800	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	Assuming that the labor market continues to improve, a key policy question for us will be how inflation developments should bear on our decision concerning the timing of liftoff.	13	1
201412	1801	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	We included a new question in the SEP to help gain some insight into your thinking on this topic, and I appreciate your willingness to provide more detailed information concerning your views both on the appropriate timing of liftoff and the economic conditions you expect to prevail at that time.	13	1
201412	1802	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	It appears from your responses that most of you anticipate that liftoff will become appropriate during the first three quarters of next year.	13	1
201412	1803	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	Many of you report that you expect core inflation will be running about 1½ percent or just a tad higher, while headline inflation will be running under or only slightly above 1 percent.	13	1
201412	1804	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	At the point that you see liftoff as appropriate, it therefore appears that most of you do not expect to have discernable evidence in hand that would confirm that inflation is actually moving back up to 2 percent.	13	1
201412	1805	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	Let me say that, like most of you, I also anticipate liftoff under conditions like these, but for me to support a decision to lift off with core inflation in the neighborhood of 1½ percent and headline inflation significantly lower, I will need to feel reasonably confident that inflation will actually begin moving back up to 2 percent over the next couple of years.	13	1
201412	1806	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	To make such a forecast, I will be relying on theory, consistent with historical evidence, that with well-anchored inflation expectations, inflation will move up as the output gap shrinks and commodity prices stabilize.	13	1
201412	1807	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	Incoming evidence confirming that inflation expectations remain well anchored, that energy and commodity prices are stabilizing, and that resource slack will continue to erode, possibly even with some small overshoot in the labor market, would bolster my confidence that inflation will, in fact, head back toward our 2 percent longer-run objective, in line with my SEP submission.	13	1
201412	1808	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	I admit this is a forecast-based approach to tightening, but I’m comfortable with this approach because, given the lags in monetary policy, I think we have to base our decisions on where we think inflation and real activity are heading and not where they are.	13	1
201412	1809	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	That said, if unfolding developments were to materially diminish my confidence in this inflation outlook, then I probably would want to be more cautious about removing accommodation.	13	1
201412	1810	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	In this regard, there are a few things I will be watching closely.	13	1
201412	1811	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	One is wage developments.	13	1
201412	1812	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	For example, as several of you mentioned, we may be seeing some tentative signs—and I’d underline “tentative”—that nominal wage growth may be stepping up.	13	1
201412	1813	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	Even though I recognize that the link between nominal wage growth and consumer price inflation is pretty weak, if a sustained step-up in nominal wage growth were to emerge, this would suggest that we’re moving closer to our full employment objective, and it would enhance my confidence that PCE inflation would move back to 2 percent.	13	1
201412	1814	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	Conversely, if nominal wage growth fails to step up at all while core PCE inflation was, for example, to move yet lower, I would be more cautious about lifting off.	13	1
201412	1815	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	Similarly, for now I consider the jury to be out on whether recent movements in TIPS breakevens reflect some broad-based reduction in confidence in our willingness and ability to achieve our 2 percent inflation objective or whether they instead reflect the transitory influence of recent oil price declines and possibly financial market spillovers from European inflation developments.	13	1
201412	1816	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	But should we see further declines in measures of inflation expectations after oil prices have leveled off, this, too, would give me pause.	13	1
201412	1817	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	With respect to the decline in inflation compensation and financial market developments more generally, I would note that a possible interpretation both of the move down in inflation compensation and also the sizable gap between our SEP  paths for the federal funds rate and the path implied by market prices is that market participants believe that the equilibrium real interest rate has declined.	13	1
201412	1818	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	Such a decline would imply a higher likelihood of periods when nominal rates will be at the zero lower bound and inflation will be below target.	13	1
201412	1819	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	If inflation is expected to be near 2 percent during normal times but below 2 percent during zero-lower-bound periods and the odds of zero-lower-bound episodes are increased, we would expect to see inflation compensation drift down.	13	1
201412	1820	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	I think this interpretation is perhaps in line with President Kocherlakota’s memo to us on this topic.	13	1
201412	1821	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	In this regard, I found the Tealbook analysis pertaining to the cost of insurance against inflation outcomes quite interesting.	13	1
201412	1822	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	It suggests that the cost of insuring against high inflation outcomes has moved down while the cost of insuring against low inflation outcomes has moved up, consistent with the decline in the equilibrium real rate.	13	1
201412	1823	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	In summary, I don’t think there’s a simple clear-cut answer to the question of whether inflation near current levels would or would not be consistent with liftoff being appropriate.	13	1
201412	1824	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	For me, the answer will depend on both the outlook for inflation at the time and our confidence in the projection.	13	1
201412	1825	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	I think the current language in paragraph 3 of alternative B is, therefore, appropriately open ended on this question.	13	1
201412	1826	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	Let me stop there.	13	1

201412	2069	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Given our imperfect understanding of wage and price dynamics, we should be flexible to move the timing of our liftoff up or back, depending on incoming data.	23	2
201412	2070	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Second, it further emphasizes that we’d be moving from time-dependent to more data- driven language as monetary policy normalizes.	23	2
201412	2071	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Third, patience is the appropriate policy for now.	23	2
201412	2072	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Nominal wage growth and price inflation have been stubbornly low.	23	2
201412	2073	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	We should wait for some evidence that inflation is more clearly on a gradual path toward our 2 percent inflation target.	23	2
201412	2074	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Certainly, lower oil prices and a stronger dollar will have some effect on the overall level of prices, but to have such little evidence of wage and price pressures indicates that we still have significant labor market slack.	23	2
201412	2075	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	The challenge is likely to be determining when to stop being patient.	23	2
201412	2076	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	I think it is very unlikely that we will have much evidence of wage and price pressures soon, certainly not at the next two meetings.	23	2
201412	2077	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	In fact, the earliest is likely to be the middle of next year.	23	2
201412	2078	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	This will be the art of the liftoff.	23	2
201412	2079	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	We want to make sure we have enough evidence that labor markets have tightened, but we must have and must appreciate the need for some insurance, given the long lags and uncertainty surrounding the effect of our first tightening.	23	2
201412	2080	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	In terms of the two questions that you have, I actually very much like the word “patient.”	23	2
201412	2081	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	I think it is an improvement.	23	2
201412	2082	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	If you define it in terms of “unlikely at the next several meetings,” it is very unlikely that we would have any evidence that wages and prices are going to be moving toward 2 percent in the next two meetings.	23	2
201412	2083	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	So I’m very comfortable with that.	23	2
201412	2084	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	If anything, even though we should look through the oil price changes, it’s going to be very hard to look through them over the next two meetings.	23	2
201412	2085	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	So I think it is very appropriate.	23	2
201412	2086	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	In terms of tying it to the SEP liftoff and providing a little more clarity as to what we want to see to take the word “patient” out, I believe that’s more difficult.	23	2
201412	2087	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	I don’t think we want to be overly specific on that.	23	2
201412	2088	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	I would want to be confident we’re moving back to 2 percent inflation, and so that’s not just labor market statistics.	23	2
201412	2089	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	It’s not just wages or prices.	23	2
201412	2090	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	It’s looking at the constellation of data that we have and saying that we have more confidence than what we’ve had over the past several years that we’re actually on the right path.	23	2
201412	2091	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	So I would not tie it to labor market markers that, at the same inflation rate and with a slightly lower unemployment rate, would be sufficient.	23	2
201412	2092	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	And I don’t think it would be sufficient just to see one piece of data on wages or prices.	23	2
201412	2093	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	We’re going to want to look at the constellation and—	23	2
201412	2094	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	Just to clarify, what I said was that we would want to be reasonably confident that inflation is moving back toward our target, even though it’s below.	23	2
201412	2095	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	I meant that to take account of exactly what you’re saying.	23	2
201412	2096	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	That’s not any simple statistic.	23	2
201412	2097	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	It’s looking at a whole constellation of factors to make that judgment.	23	2
201412	2098	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Yes.	23	2
201412	2099	2014-12-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	If we’re reasonably confident that we’re back on the path toward the 2 percent inflation rate, I would be comfortable with that.	23	2

201412	2101	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	President Evans.	23	2
201412	2102	2014-12-17	meeting	EVANS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201412	2103	2014-12-17	meeting	EVANS	I can support alternative B today as offered, because it’s merely a modest restatement of our current patient policy strategy without committing to a date-based future action.	23	2
201412	2104	2014-12-17	meeting	EVANS	That said, I expect the public to quickly embrace June 2015 as the focal point for our eventual policy liftoff, and I’m uncomfortable with that assessment today as I read the economic situation.	23	2
201412	2105	2014-12-17	meeting	EVANS	After six years of inflation averaging 1½ percent, I would prefer a course of action that maximizes our likelihood of achieving 2 percent inflation by 2017 at the latest, and we need to hit our price-stability objective in a sustainable manner, not simply as a short-term burst of transitory relative price adjustments when oil prices bounce back.	23	2
201412	2106	2014-12-17	meeting	EVANS	Given my assessment of the economy’s fundamentals, I myself will be surprised if it becomes appropriate to begin increasing short-term policy rates before March 2016.	23	2
201412	2107	2014-12-17	meeting	EVANS	But things can change—I recognize that.	23	2
201412	2108	2014-12-17	meeting	EVANS	Within this context, I prefer the conditional language in paragraph 3ʹ of alternative A.	23	2
201412	2109	2014-12-17	meeting	EVANS	Its conditionality with respect to achieving our price-stability mandate is much clearer, and I believe the public would better infer that we intend to achieve our 2 percent inflation objective sooner rather than later.	23	2
201412	2110	2014-12-17	meeting	EVANS	At a time when the Bank of Japan and the ECB are struggling at the zero lower bound with low inflation, there’s no more powerful tool available than a strong and credible public expectation of actions to achieve this better outcome.	23	2
201412	2111	2014-12-17	meeting	EVANS	This is an important preventive defense for ourselves.	23	2
201412	2112	2014-12-17	meeting	EVANS	Without such a marker, I fear that the focal point for liftoff will be too firmly date-based on June 2015, without enough data conditionality, in the event our inflation improvements stall.	23	2
201412	2113	2014-12-17	meeting	EVANS	I did like very much some of the suggestions that President Lockhart made in terms of trying to push a little further into the future the start of our normalization.	23	2
201412	2114	2014-12-17	meeting	EVANS	Madam Chair, yesterday you listed a number of policy caveats related to this conditionality test.	23	2
201412	2115	2014-12-17	meeting	EVANS	I believe my own list is well aligned with your comments.	23	2
201412	2116	2014-12-17	meeting	EVANS	For me to envision a June 2015 liftoff as the appropriate response to economic conditions, I would like to see a number of developments—first, continued strong employment growth, associated improvements in other labor market indicators, and continued growth above potential.	23	2
201412	2117	2014-12-17	meeting	EVANS	Second, I’d want to see clear signs that wages were beginning to increase toward the range of 3 to 4 percent that I associate with neutral cost pressures.	23	2
201412	2118	2014-12-17	meeting	EVANS	I think this is important for reinforcing the evidence that resource gaps have been sufficiently narrowed and for establishing cost increases that would be more consistent with an underlying inflation rate of 2 percent.	23	2
201412	2119	2014-12-17	meeting	EVANS	The third important condition would be an increase in TIPS-based inflation expectations from today’s low levels.	23	2
201412	2120	2014-12-17	meeting	EVANS	As you and President Kocherlakota mentioned yesterday, there are serious costs when we live in a world with low inflation, a low equilibrium real rate, and monetary policy stuck at the zero lower bound.	23	2
201412	2121	2014-12-17	meeting	EVANS	If market measures of inflation compensation are lower today because the market participants are much more mindful of and averse to these costly low-inflation scenarios, then the FOMC should better ensure that we hit our 2 percent objective with greater confidence and more quickly.	23	2
201412	2122	2014-12-17	meeting	EVANS	The final signal I would be looking for would be an increase in my inflation projection to 2 percent in 2017 at the latest under the contemplated post-liftoff path.	23	2
201412	2123	2014-12-17	meeting	EVANS	As you suggested yesterday, Madam Chair, there is a risk that core and underlying inflation measures could become persistently too low owing to relative price downdrafts outside of our control.	23	2
201412	2124	2014-12-17	meeting	EVANS	You mentioned that you would be monitoring for things like that.	23	2
201412	2125	2014-12-17	meeting	EVANS	It’s not your base case, of course.	23	2
201412	2126	2014-12-17	meeting	EVANS	In this case, inflation’s behavior would likely be inconsistent with our price-stability objective, in my opinion.	23	2
201412	2127	2014-12-17	meeting	EVANS	We thus may still need to reinforce our patient, data-conditional policy messages along the path in order to keep inflation up.	23	2
201412	2128	2014-12-17	meeting	EVANS	It’s certainly possible that these caveats will be overcome by mid-2015.	23	2
201412	2129	2014-12-17	meeting	EVANS	That’s part of the conditionality test.	23	2
201412	2130	2014-12-17	meeting	EVANS	Still, I continue to worry that we’re hoping to thread the needle and bring inflation up to 2 percent from below without ever crossing over 2 percent.	23	2
201412	2131	2014-12-17	meeting	EVANS	I think this hopeful scenario is fraught with risks that inflation will stall out before we get to 2 percent.	23	2
201412	2132	2014-12-17	meeting	EVANS	If confronted with a choice of stalling at 1½ or 1¾ percent inflation versus modestly overshooting inflation at 2¼ to 2½ percent inflation for a time, I firmly believe that the latter is more consistent with our stated long-run strategy for monetary policy.	23	2
201412	2133	2014-12-17	meeting	EVANS	Now, on the questions that you asked, I think your characterization of the liftoff dates is accurate—almost all participants in 2015.	23	2
201412	2134	2014-12-17	meeting	EVANS	I don’t disagree with that.	23	2

201412	2142	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	For some time I’ve argued that, as we approach a more normal policy-setting environment, we should be moving our forward guidance away from date-based guidance to more state-contingent guidance describing the conditions we deem important in determining appropriate policy.	23	2
201412	2143	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	In reformulating the forward guidance, over time, I believe we should strive to remove the focus from the date of a policy change to the conditions we look at in determining actual and projected progress of the economy toward our goals.	23	2
201412	2144	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	Chair Yellen’s remarks yesterday, on the economic conditions and indicators she’ll be looking at in coming months to inform her view of when to lift off, seemed a very good way to frame the discussion—perhaps not doable in the statement, but something to strive for in our public discourse and around the table.	23	2
201412	2145	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	Similarly, at our October meeting, we took an important step in the right direction in our statement by adding the qualifier that the timing of liftoff would vary if incoming information suggested either faster- or slower-than-anticipated progress toward our goals.	23	2
201412	2146	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	With the end of the asset purchase program, with market participants expecting some type of change in guidance, and with the Chair holding a postmeeting press conference, we have a unique opportunity to take a further step today to clarify our policy expectations.	23	2

201412	2154	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	Looking ahead, based on the economic progress that’s been made and my forecast of continued progress, I believe the time for lifting off from the zero lower bound is nearing, and we have to do our best to prepare the public and markets for it.	23	2
201412	2155	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	The SEP suggests the consensus among participants is that liftoff is going to be in the first half of the year provided the economy evolves as anticipated.	23	2

201412	2157	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	Monetary policy will, of course, remain extremely accommodative for some time to come, even after the first rate increase.	23	2
201412	2158	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	And I think that’s something that we need to inform the public of as well.	23	2
201412	2159	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	Yet, of course, liftoff will certainly be a historic event, given the journey the economy and monetary policy have been on for the past six years.	23	2
201412	2160	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	The Committee always has to balance several considerations when it begins contemplating a change in policy direction.	23	2
201412	2161	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	But, in the current circumstances, these considerations are heightened.	23	2
201412	2162	2014-12-17	meeting	MESTER	We’ve seen several false starts, when it looked as though the economy was poised to accelerate, only to slow down again.	23	2

201412	2174	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	President Bullard.	23	2
201412	2175	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2

201412	2177	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	I’m going to talk about three topics.	23	2
201412	2178	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	One is that the constellation of data that we face today is not consistent with a policy rate pinned down at the zero lower bound, and, for this reason, I think it’s important for the Committee to be considering normalization strategies.	23	2
201412	2179	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	So I’ll talk about that a little bit.	23	2
201412	2180	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	The second topic is that inflation expectations are falling.	23	2
201412	2181	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	I think this is of paramount concern for a central bank.	23	2
201412	2182	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	Inflation expectations should not fall over a horizon as long as 5 to 10 years.	23	2
201412	2183	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	We need to be ready to react to this, if necessary.	23	2
201412	2184	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	Frankly, I don’t think that we’re ready to react to this.	23	2
201412	2185	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	Third, our policy options today are cementing date-dependent policy.	23	2
201412	2186	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	I agree with President Evans on this, and I have some suggestions about how to move toward more state-contingency by creating windows of meetings at which the Committee may potentially move, instead of single meetings.	23	2
201412	2187	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	On the first topic, concerning the constellation of data, unemployment is only a few ticks away from our own estimates of the natural rate.	23	2
201412	2188	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	If you’d rather look at indexes of labor market performance, they are also not far from their long-run averages.	23	2
201412	2189	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	Inflation is only a few ticks away from our target.	23	2
201412	2190	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	Constructing a quadratic objective in inflation and unemployment deviations, as we have in St Louis, shows that this Committee is closer to achieving its goals than at about 90 percent of the Committee meetings that have occurred since 1960.	23	2
201412	2191	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	So I think the idea that we’re far away from our goals is false.	23	2
201412	2192	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	The policy stance, on the other hand, is to have the policy rate still near zero and liftoff still some time away.	23	2
201412	2193	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	The policy stance is dramatically different from what it has been for similar data constellations in the past.	23	2
201412	2194	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	We have a large balance sheet, and we have a zero interest rate policy.	23	2
201412	2195	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	From this perspective, our policy is badly out of position compared with historical norms.	23	2
201412	2196	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	For this reason, I want to push back against those who believe it’s inappropriate to be thinking about normalization.	23	2
201412	2197	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	It’s totally appropriate to be thinking about normalization now and at coming meetings.	23	2
201412	2198	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	The second topic is that inflation expectations are falling, and I don’t think we should be making as many excuses about this as we are at this meeting.	23	2
201412	2199	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	The experience in Japan over the past 20 years and in the euro area today shows that allowing expectations of inflation over longer-term horizons to fall can create unique and very difficult problems for central banks.	23	2
201412	2200	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	We need to be prepared, although it’s not my baseline case, to make a move—and possibly a dramatic move—to shore up inflation expectations, if that becomes necessary, over the next six months.	23	2
201412	2201	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	Probably the most potent tool we have at this point, given that QE is out of the picture, would be to delay the date of liftoff.	23	2
201412	2202	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	As many of you know, I have argued in the past that promising to stay at zero even longer can be counterproductive with regard to inflation expectations, and so if we have to do this, I want to do it in a particular way.	23	2
201412	2203	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	If we have to delay liftoff at some point in order to shore up longer-run expectations, I would prefer to do that in reaction to bullish data on the economy, as opposed to weakening data on the economy.	23	2
201412	2204	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	That would send a signal that it’s the expectations of inflation we care about, and it’s not sending the signal that we think the economy is going to be weaker in the future, and that we’re reacting to that.	23	2
201412	2205	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	This has been a very difficult issue for the Committee over the past five years, but, if we have to play that card, that’s the way I would prefer to play it.	23	2
201412	2206	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	That would avoid the negative feedback that could otherwise occur—we’re delaying liftoff because we see a weaker economy in the second half of 2015 or out into 2016, and we see even lower inflation numbers.	23	2
201412	2207	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	That process can become self-fulfilling and lead to a bad equilibrium, and that’s exactly what we’re trying to avoid.	23	2
201412	2208	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	So I would just put that out there as a possible contingency if the inflation expectations situation does not turn around in the next six months.	23	2
201412	2209	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	There is a fairly substantial risk that inflation will continue to decline—and that, possibly, inflation expectations will continue to decline—in the months ahead.	23	2
201412	2210	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	The third topic is that our policy choices today are cementing too much date dependency.	23	2
201412	2211	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	The probabilities of action by this Committee are totally piling up on June.	23	2
201412	2212	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	The primary dealer survey put no weight on meetings other than meetings that had a press conference attached, and put most weight on the June meeting as a possible date of liftoff.	23	2
201412	2213	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	I think it’s particularly telling that we have a lot of weight on the June meeting—no primary dealers, or maybe only one, on the April meeting, and none on the July meeting.	23	2
201412	2214	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	So, ideally, as we’re sitting here today, we should see a spread-out probability structure of three possible meetings.	23	2
201412	2215	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	I’m going to suggest a way to do that here.	23	2
201412	2216	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	What are the dangers with putting all of your eggs in the June basket?	23	2
201412	2217	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	I think one of the main dangers for the Committee is that the data running up to the June meeting aren’t ideal or aren’t what we’re hoping for.	23	2
201412	2218	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	Of course, if they are, everything will go smoothly.	23	2
201412	2219	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	I’m talking about the case in which they’re not.	23	2
201412	2220	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	Suppose we get somewhat weaker data during that period.	23	2
201412	2221	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	Then, should the Committee decide to plow ahead, even with less-than-desirable data, that can erode the credibility of the Committee that policy is state dependent, because what you’re doing is saying, “We’re going to move in June even if the data don’t agree with us.”	23	2
201412	2222	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	And then people start to think that we’re not sufficiently attentive to incoming data on the economy.	23	2
201412	2223	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	I also would like to reiterate that I think this harms the natural decisionmaking process on the Committee.	23	2
201412	2224	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	A lot of the compromise on the Committee has to do with trading off things that you might do at one meeting versus doing them at the next meeting or possibly pulling them earlier.	23	2
201412	2225	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	Because of our press conference structure, it puts a lot of pressure on certain meetings.	23	2
201412	2226	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	Members of the Committee feel as though, if they’re going to get something done, they want to get it done at a particular meeting, and it hardens positions, I think, relative to what they would otherwise be.	23	2
201412	2227	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	My solution is that we have press conferences associated with every meeting.	23	2
201412	2228	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	At this point, I’m not going to insert the passionate speech about press conferences at every meeting that I’ve given at other meetings in the past, but I’ll reiterate a little bit of it here.	23	2
201412	2229	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	I think you could announce today, even at the press conference, that we’re going to have press conferences at every meeting in 2015, or you could say, “I would contemplate having press conferences at every meeting in 2015.”	23	2
201412	2230	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	This would put all of the dates on the table.	23	2
201412	2231	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	It would spread out the probabilities the way I’m talking about.	23	2
201412	2232	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	It would make all meetings ex ante identical and distribute the probability of a liftoff move more or less equally among April, June, and July instead of just June.	23	2
201412	2233	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	It would create a window for possible action by the Committee.	23	2
201412	2234	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	The Committee could then walk into one of those meetings at which the data were relatively favorable and say, “Okay.	23	2
201412	2235	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	We’re ready to go at this meeting.”	23	2
201412	2236	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	I don’t think it would matter much in any of those three meetings, in a macroeconomic sense, as long as we got going on the normalization process.	23	2
201412	2237	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	But it would allow us to move when the data speak to that possibility, instead of having to possibly move against what the data are telling us at a particular meeting.	23	2
201412	2238	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	This would mitigate, in my mind, some of the risk of a liftoff event that would be harkening back to the June 2013 meeting and its aftermath, in which, I think, the Committee felt a lot of pressure to do something at that meeting, as opposed to waiting until the August meeting.	23	2
201412	2239	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	I don’t believe the Committee was quite ready.	23	2
201412	2240	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	We put a lot of pressure on the press conference.	23	2
201412	2241	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	The ultimate reaction of that was that the Committee came off as quite a bit more hawkish than it probably was, and we ended up with the taper tantrum and its effects in the summer of 2013.	23	2
201412	2242	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	You could mitigate quite a bit of this by creating this window of possible meetings at which we could move.	23	2
201412	2243	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	I do not think that the prospect of a surprise press conference fixes the situation, because this is mostly about expectations, as we sit here today, about when the Committee will move.	23	2
201412	2244	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	It’s true that we could move at any time.	23	2
201412	2245	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	Of course, we can call a meeting at any time and take action at any time, but we would want to do that only in particularly dire circumstances, and it would shock markets to do that.	23	2
201412	2246	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	So I don’t think the fact that we could call a press conference would fix the problem of expectations, which are really piling up on June at this point.	23	2
201412	2247	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	I have just a couple of further comments.	23	2
201412	2248	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	One is that, Madam Chair, you asked for comments on defining “patience” as “at least the next couple of meetings.”	23	2
201412	2249	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	Here I’d like to associate myself with the comments of President Williams, which I thought were very good.	23	2
201412	2250	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	“Patient” could be interpreted as “a very long time.”	23	2
201412	2251	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	Even if you define it in the press conference, there’ll still be market chatter that will continue in the coming weeks, and it might have the effect of pushing out expectations of liftoff.	23	2
201412	2252	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	So that’s a risk that we face.	23	2
201412	2253	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	I think you need to push back hard against that in the press conference in order to get this to be right.	23	2
201412	2254	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	I also agree with President Williams that we should define things in the statement and not in press conference comments.	23	2
201412	2255	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	If it is, in fact, the policy of the Committee, we should define it here at the Committee.	23	2
201412	2256	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	It leaves ambiguity to put too much pressure on the press conference, and, at some points in the past—in particular, June 2013—it didn’t work out very well.	23	2
201412	2257	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	Let me bring up one other problem with the “patient” language that I think needs to be addressed.	23	2
201412	2258	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	By using “patience” and then defining it as “the next couple of meetings,” we’re harkening back to the 2004–06 tightening cycle, which is not something I would prefer to do.	23	2
201412	2259	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	I do not believe that that tightening cycle was very successful in the end.	23	2
201412	2260	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	The bursting of the housing bubble caused global macroeconomic disaster, from which we’re still trying to recover.	23	2
201412	2261	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	So, saying that we’re going to use “patient” in the same way that we used it in 2004 will immediately trigger a lot of discussion that we’re going to do the whole tightening cycle the way we did it in the period from 2004 to 2006, which involved moves of 25 basis points at 17 consecutive meetings and was way too mechanical and not data dependent enough.	23	2
201412	2262	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	So I would encourage you, Madam Chair, to push back against the interpretation that this is a repeat of the 2004–06 tightening cycle.	23	2
201412	2263	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	And, really, all of us should push back against that interpretation because I don’t think that that was a successful tightening cycle.	23	2
201412	2264	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	Finally, my last comment on the word “patient” is that, if we include “patient” in there, which I think we will, taking “patient” out is actually the tightening move.	23	2
201412	2265	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	As soon as you take “patient” out, it means that action is imminent.	23	2
201412	2266	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	This is a general problem with this kind of approach, and that can’t be fixed.	23	2
201412	2267	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	The Committee should be aware of this.	23	2
201412	2268	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	Once you say you’re going to take “patient” out, you’re basically committing to future action, except, perhaps, in dire circumstances in which the data go in a dramatically different direction.	23	2
201412	2269	2014-12-17	meeting	BULLARD	Thanks for the opportunity to comment, Madam Chair.	23	2

201412	2456	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	This is obviously not going to be my preferred policy path, but I thought you did a good job yesterday of describing the conditions that are likely to prevail.	23	2

201412	2459	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	One is, it would be better if we were to be planning more strategically about what post-liftoff policy is going to look like.	23	2

201412	2464	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	If we build this up too much externally, communicating that liftoff is a historic event and we’re finally liberating the US economy from the chains that it’s been in for the past eight years, that makes it very challenging for us to reverse course after liftoff.	23	2

201412	2466	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The first is planning more strategically within the Committee for what we’re going to be doing after liftoff, and then the second is communicating, I think, about what that strategy is likely to be.	23	2
201412	2467	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The second piece I wanted to comment on concerns my thinking.	23	2
201412	2468	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I believe it’s useful to tie back our policy recommendations to our consensus statement.	23	2
201412	2469	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	So I want to say a couple of things about the maximum-employment mandate.	23	2

201412	2474	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	But my thinking about the employment mandate is basically asymmetric.	23	2
201412	2475	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I don’t believe that it was included in the Federal Reserve Act as a way to tighten policy.	23	2
201412	2476	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	It’s fundamentally in there as a way to provide a way to ease policy relative to what would be true if we had only a price-stability mandate.	23	2
201412	2477	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	More colloquially, no one is going to complain to the Federal Reserve, “You’ve created way too many jobs.	23	2
201412	2478	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Stop creating so many jobs.”	23	2
201412	2479	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	That’s what promoting maximum employment means— trying to make jobs as high as you can, given you’ve got a price-stability mandate.	23	2
201412	2480	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	So the growth in employment is very welcome.	23	2

201412	2499	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	There is risk to that outlook, as Governor Fischer reminded us yesterday.	23	2
201412	2500	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We should be thinking about this.	23	2

201412	2502	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The staff projection means that in the staff’s assessment, in any of the next four years, the probability of inflation’s being below target is larger than 50 percent.	23	2
201412	2503	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	If we weight that, as our Minneapolis memo encouraged us to do, by what kinds of real conditions associated with those low-inflation outcomes are likely to prevail, I think you would be driven to say that the likelihood of low inflation is larger even than 50 percent.	23	2
201412	2504	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Fact 1:  We’ve had low, below-target inflation for 30 months.	23	2
201412	2505	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Fact 2:  Future inflation looks as though it’s going to be low, according to the staff forecast, for four years.	23	2

201412	2508	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Because of the decline in longer-term inflation expectations in the past few months, at least as reflected in the market-based measures, the Committee has not been able to make this assertion in the past two FOMC statements—and in the one that I suspect will be issued today.	23	2
201412	2509	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	What is a proposed response to these three facts—low inflation for the past two and a half years, low inflation for the next four years, and declining long-term inflation expectations?	23	2
201412	2510	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The proposed response to these three facts in alternative B is to communicate that the FOMC is continuing on the path of gradual removal of accommodation that it initiated a year ago—or, more arguably, in May 2013.	23	2
201412	2511	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In my assessment, the FOMC’s failure to respond to weak inflation runs the risk of creating a harmful downward slide in inflation and inflation expectations of the kind that we have seen in Japan and Europe.	23	2
201412	2512	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I’ll emphasize again that I see this as a risk.	23	2

201412	2514	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I see this risk as unacceptable, given how hard it would be for the FOMC to respond successfully if this risk did, in fact, materialize.	23	2

201412	2516	2014-12-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	But my preferred response would be for the FOMC to communicate that it’ll keep the target range for the fed funds rate unchanged as long as the one-to-two-year-ahead outlook for the inflation rate remains below 2 percent.	23	2

201412	2635	2014-12-17	meeting	FISCHER	I think, as somebody who wasn’t here before, that we are doing things in a different way—with more consensus, more efforts to reach a consensus, and models that have advanced significantly since, say, 20 years ago and even since 2004—and that we’re operating on a new basis.	23	2
201412	2636	2014-12-17	meeting	FISCHER	In that basis, we’ll find every decision as complicated as this one, and we should start making it clear to the world that that’s the situation.	23	2
201412	2637	2014-12-17	meeting	FISCHER	That means that we need to turn our attention and that of the staff, whose technical expertise I value more and more every day, even more to the technical issues that will arise as we normalize, including how to coordinate the use of our two interest rate instruments and when to begin asset sales, which we’ve left on the side, although there was considerable praise yesterday from President Fisher for this memo that was sent around by the Desk.	23	2
