201412	2725	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	I think it’s appropriate at this time to start to prepare the public—the markets, really—for the onset of normalization.	23	2
201412	2726	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	There could easily be a reaction in the markets after this statement.	23	2
201412	2727	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	I think that would be appropriate.	23	2
201412	2728	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	Turning to your two questions at the beginning of this round, Madam Chair, I’m okay with your definition of “patient.”	23	2
201412	2729	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	I do think we need a shorter-handled tool, in a way.	23	2
201412	2730	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	“Considerable time” was really a six-month tool.	23	2
201412	2731	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	“Patient” is really a two-meeting tool.	23	2
201412	2732	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	I realize that’s time based and kind of awkward, but it’s also swimming in a sea of data dependency and seems to work, and we should do what works.	23	2
201412	2733	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	In terms of leaving meetings on the table, I’ll conclude with this thought:  It’s really a bad idea to think that we could raise rates and do it in the sense of calling a press conference suddenly at the end of a meeting or the day of a meeting.	23	2
201412	2734	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	That is not a way I would go at all.	23	2
201412	2735	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	I just think it can’t be that important to do it.	23	2
201412	2736	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	It would have to be really important to raise rates then rather than seven weeks later.	23	2
201412	2737	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	It would be a big surprise to the market.	23	2
201412	2738	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	This is a tremendously important event in our history, and it ought not to be thrown together in that way.	23	2
201412	2739	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	So I guess I would offer for consideration a thought that, if it’s a close call in March, then there would be an option to put April on the table, and maybe July as well, at that time, but well in advance.	23	2
201412	2740	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	If we’re going to put April on the table, I wouldn’t do it on the day of the meeting.	23	2
201412	2741	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	I would do it as part of the March meeting so that we don’t surprise the market.	23	2
201412	2742	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	As I said, it’s really critical that we be transparent.	23	2
201412	2743	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	The market will come to understand what we’re going to do if we’re transparent and predictable, and that’s tremendously important in this process.	23	2
201412	2744	2014-12-17	meeting	POWELL	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201412	2745	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	23	2
201412	2746	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Brainard.	23	2
201412	2747	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Thank you.	23	2
201412	2748	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Since we last met, we have seen two strong payroll reports, and the labor market is clearly continuing to strengthen, which is very welcome.	23	2
201412	2749	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	But, of course, we also see continued risks associated with below-target inflation, with some deterioration in market-based measures of inflation expectations and this taking place against a global backdrop, which is broadly disinflationary.	23	2
201412	2750	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	What does this mean for policy?	23	2
201412	2751	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	First, it’s important to acknowledge that the continued underlying momentum in the economy validates the pace of tapering and the end of asset purchases.	23	2
201412	2752	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	That’s a very welcome change from previous attempts to end unconventional policy.	23	2
201412	2753	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Second, conditions overall, I think, validate our strategy of remaining somewhat cautious on the removal of monetary accommodation, although I believe we can acknowledge that the date of liftoff is now coming more clearly into view.	23	2
201412	2754	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	For my part, I think market expectations are nicely aligned with our outlook on the appropriate timing of liftoff, which makes me quite cautious about any change in wording that could perturb current expectations.	23	2
201412	2755	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	The danger is that markets take signal from the change in wording when none is intended, and, of course, we know from past experience how disruptive unintended signals can be.	23	2
201412	2756	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	As a result, I would probably have been more comfortable leaving the existing forward guidance anchored and making the outlook section of the statement do more of the work.	23	2
201412	2757	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	I think I would not have been inclined to introduce a new qualitative concept.	23	2
201412	2758	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	I worry, in particular, that the choice of the word “patient” could be read as suggesting the same timing and pace of tightening as the last time the word was used, neither of which is appropriate to today’s conditions.	23	2
201412	2759	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	However, I think we all recognize that many around this table did not like the existing language and were very uncomfortable keeping it, and, under those constraints, I think the language in alternative B is as good an approach as any of the alternatives.	23	2
201412	2760	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	In particular, I would give my vote to the Chair in navigating these shoals and gently guiding market expectations using the press conference.	23	2
201412	2761	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	With regard to the outlook, the main takeaways on the outlook for the full employment part of the dual mandate are captured well by paragraphs 1 and 2.	23	2
201412	2762	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	I would also be inclined to drop the word “somewhat.”	23	2
201412	2763	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Describing the recent data and outlook for inflation is trickier.	23	2
201412	2764	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	I still believe, in light of recent data, that, as resource slack diminishes further, inflation is likely to move back up toward our 2 percent goal, but the risks to that outlook are clearly on the downside.	23	2
201412	2765	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	So I think it’s right to note, as alternative B does, some concern about the inflation outlook and just to recognize that, if we were in the same circumstances with a sharp increase in the price of oil and as far away from the 2 percent target above it as we are currently below it, we would certainly note that in our statement.	23	2
201412	2766	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	I believe it’s appropriate to do that here.	23	2
201412	2767	2014-12-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201412	2768	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	23	2
201412	2769	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	Well, thank you all for your—	23	2
201412	2770	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	You’ve got one more.	23	2
201412	2771	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	Oh, sorry.	23	2
201412	2772	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	My deepest apologies.	23	2
201412	2773	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	No worries.	23	2
201412	2774	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	It happened one time under Chairman Bernanke’s watch, too.	23	2
201412	2775	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	So you can do it once.	23	2
201412	2776	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	[Laughter.]	23	2
201412	2777	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	I support alternative B, and I am comfortable with what the Chair proposes to communicate at the press conference in terms of the “patient” language.	23	2
201412	2778	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	I think “at least the next couple of meetings” is a good way of characterizing it.	23	2
201412	2779	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Also, the way you propose to characterize the participants’ views for 2015 sounds very good to me.	23	2
201412	2780	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Before I get into the statement language, I do want to make some more general observations about monetary policy.	23	2
201412	2781	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	First, in terms of my own thinking, I believe the likely timing of liftoff has moved in somewhat, given the strength of the recent data and the fact that I have greater confidence now that that momentum will be sustained in 2015.	23	2
201412	2782	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	So it’s not just having strong employment reports, but also being more confident that the momentum will be sustained.	23	2
201412	2783	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Before, I was putting more of my weight on June than other meetings, but my expectations were more skewed June or later.	23	2
201412	2784	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Now I would say that I see June as more of a midpoint, with the probability weight of June also increasing somewhat.	23	2
201412	2785	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	The important question in my mind, as I talked about yesterday, is how much weight to give to the decline in inflation that’s been generated by this sharp drop in energy prices.	23	2
201412	2786	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	My own bias has been mostly to look through that decline as long as the decline does not lead to a fall in wage compensation and other recent nominal income trends are largely undisturbed, and provided that inflation expectations remain broadly anchored.	23	2
201412	2787	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	To date, I view these two conditions as still in place, and, because lower oil prices are likely to be a net positive for growth, that’s also important, as it increases my confidence in the sustainability of the expansion.	23	2
201412	2788	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	So, for the time being, I’m very much looking through the decline in oil prices, although that could change in light of future developments.	23	2
201412	2789	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Second, in terms of this issue of being patient with respect to the timing of liftoff, not in terms of the statement language but more as a general concept, I think it’s also important not to be too patient.	23	2
201412	2790	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	For example, some argue—and I’ve made the argument myself—that it would be less risky to be a little bit late rather than a bit early in terms of the timing of liftoff.	23	2
201412	2791	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	I still agree with that, but I do think it’s important not to push that idea too far.	23	2
201412	2792	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	In particular, if we were too late and the unemployment rate were to fall considerably below the natural rate, inflation could rise substantially above our 2 percent objective.	23	2
201412	2793	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	I understand that the Phillips curve is very flat, so there’s a low probability of this happening.	23	2
201412	2794	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	But this rests on the very strong assumption that inflation expectations will remain well anchored even at very low unemployment rates, and I’m just not sure that that’s actually the case.	23	2
201412	2795	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	If the unemployment rate fell very low, the Phillips curve would steepen, and so there’s a risk in that.	23	2
201412	2796	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Now, some argue that, if that happened, we have the tools to deal with that situation.	23	2
201412	2797	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	I think that’s true, but if we’re late, we would really have to make monetary policy tight in order to push the unemployment rate up, and that would be quite problematic.	23	2
201412	2798	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	The staff memo talks about the fact that, in the postwar period, every time the unemployment rate has risen four-tenths of 1 percent or more on a three-month moving-average basis, the US economy has tumbled back into recession.	23	2
201412	2799	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	That’s not something that I want to revisit any time soon, because I don’t think I want to probe the zero lower bound again, at least during my tenure.	23	2
201412	2800	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Third, I believe it’s desirable to get off the zero lower bound as long as we think we can do so safely.	23	2
201412	2801	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Although we refer to a rise in the federal funds rate target as a tightening of monetary policy—and this harkens back to what Stan was saying—there’s a problem there in terms of talking about the tightening of monetary policy, because all that the first hikes are going to do is to be a very slight removal of a very high level of accommodation.	23	2
201412	2802	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	So I think we need to emphasize that fact in our communications—that even after the initial few tightening moves, monetary policy will still be very supportive of economic activity.	23	2
201412	2803	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Fourth, in terms of how fast to go once we begin to raise the federal funds rate, obviously, the economic news will be very important.	23	2
201412	2804	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	But how financial market conditions evolve is going to be important as well, and this deserves more emphasis in terms of our communications.	23	2
201412	2805	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	The linkage of monetary policy to the real economy works through the transmission channel of financial market conditions.	23	2
201412	2806	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	So if it’s like the taper-tantrum episode and if financial conditions were to tighten significantly with the first rate hike, then we should go more slowly, everything else being equal.	23	2
201412	2807	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Conversely, if financial conditions don’t tighten at all, which has been the situation since we began to end the asset purchase program, then we need to move more quickly.	23	2
201412	2808	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	And I think we need to get market participants sensitized to this—that financial market conditions are going to be an important factor in our thinking in terms of the monetary policy normalization process.	23	2
201412	2809	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	If they internalize the importance of financial market conditions in our own thinking, this would presumably reduce the risk of unusually large movements in financial market conditions in response to our actions.	23	2
201412	2810	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	This would be a good outcome, at least initially, because our control of financial market conditions might be quite poor at first.	23	2
201412	2811	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	In my mind, raising short-term rates for the first time in more than six years is a substantial regime shift.	23	2
201412	2812	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Finally, given all of the uncertainties about how financial conditions will respond at liftoff, I do think it’s important that we try to have liftoff occur with as little drama as possible.	23	2
201412	2813	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	There’s already going to be plenty of drama in lifting off with a new set of tools and in a regime shift of raising short-term rates after more than six years at the zero lower bound.	23	2
201412	2814	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	So I do think we want to foreshadow the expected timing of tightening as much as is feasible, subject to the inherent uncertainties of the economic outlook.	23	2
201412	2815	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	In an ideal scenario, the initial rate hike would occur precisely when it’s broadly expected.	23	2
201412	2816	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	This would work best to minimize the risks of another taper tantrum and minimize the risks of disruption to global financial markets.	23	2
201412	2817	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	It also might help minimize the risks of the types of large-scale capital flow reversals that we saw in 2013 that made life particularly difficult for some emerging market economies.	23	2
201412	2818	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Turning now to the statement, I think we want the statement to be read as modestly hawkish, reinforcing the notion that June, conditional on the data coming in relatively close to our expectations, is becoming more likely.	23	2
201412	2819	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	The Chair can reinforce this at the press conference.	23	2
201412	2820	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	The statement generally does this, and, particularly, it seems a little bit more positive about the growth outlook.	23	2
201412	2821	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	It doesn’t overemphasize the fact that inflation is below our objective, noting in paragraph 2 that inflation is expected to move back toward target.	23	2
201412	2822	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	We could even be a little bit more positive on the growth side in paragraph 1, but I can accept it as written.	23	2
201412	2823	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	I would take out the word “somewhat” because I do think we want to indicate that we really have upgraded our outlook a little bit.	23	2
201412	2824	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	So I definitely would support that.	23	2
201412	2825	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Getting the right message on inflation is very important right now because a lot of market participants are unclear about how much weight we will give to inflation in determining the timing of liftoff.	23	2
201412	2826	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	We need to make it very clear that we don’t have an inflation threshold.	23	2
201412	2827	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	In other words, there’s not a requirement that inflation must be moving up at the time of liftoff.	23	2
201412	2828	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Instead, we just must expect that inflation will rise in the future back to our 2 percent objective.	23	2
201412	2829	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Liftoff is about lessening the degree of extreme monetary accommodation, and, of course, you want to begin this process well before employment and inflation reach your objectives.	23	2
201412	2830	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	I believe many market participants are confused about this, and that explains some of the difference between what we think we’re going to do and what market participants expect for this.	23	2
201412	2831	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	So I think we have to work on that a little bit.	23	2
201412	2832	2014-12-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201412	2833	2014-12-17	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	23	2
